Proof 3: Contextual Coherence of Divine Power and Dominion
Razi's third proof based on contextual consistency of surrounding verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the surrounding verses' theme of divine power and greatness demands that the istiwa' verse be interpreted as domination, not physical settling.

Core Idea
The context of divine power and majesty requires interpreting 'istawa' as complete domination, not sitting.

Razi's third proof looks at the broader context. The verses before and after the istiwa' verse speak of Allah's perfect power, creation, and dominion. If istiwa' were literal sitting, it would be a foreign interruption. But interpreting it as 'complete domination' (istila') fits seamlessly. This lesson explores that contextual argument.

Guided Path
1
Note the themes
Identify the themes in the surrounding verses: creation, power, and ownership.
Q20:4 and Q20:6 both emphasize divine attributes.
2
Compare interpretations
Consider how literal sitting is irrelevant to these themes, while domination (istila) matches perfectly.
3
Conclude
Understand why Razi says this interpretation is 'awla (more appropriate).
Contextual consistency is a key principle of tafsir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثاني : أن نتكلم عن كل واحد من هذه الوجوه على سبيل التفصيل :
أما الذي تمسكوا به أولا . وهو الآيات السنة الدالة على استواء الله تعالى على العرش. فنقول : إنه لا يجوز أن يكون مراد الله تعالى من ذلك الاستواء : هو الاستقرار على العرش . ويدل عليه وجوه :
الأول : إن ما قبل هذه الآية، وهو قوله تعالى: « تنزيلا ممن خلق الأرض والسموات العلى »، قد بينا أن هذه الآية تدل على أنه تعالى غير مختص بشيء من الأحياز والجهات .
الثاني : إن ما بعد هذه الآية ، وهو قوله تعالى: « له ما في السموات وما في الأرض »، قد بينا : أن السماء هو الذي فيه سمو وفوقية ، فكل ما كان في جهة فوق ، فهو سماء . وإذا كان كذلك ، فقوله : « له ما في السموات وما في الأرض »، يقتضي أن كل ما كان حاصلا في جهة فوق ، كان في السماء . وإذا كان كذلك ، فقوله : « له ما في السموات وما في الأرض »، يقتضي أن كل ما كان حاصلا في جهة فوق ، فهو ملك الله تعالى ومملوك له . فلو كان تعالى مختصا بجهة فوق ، لزم كونه مملوكا لنفسه من غير محل وهو محال . فثبت : أن ما قبل قوله « الرحمن على العرش استوى » وما بعده ينفي كونه سبحانه وتعالى مختصا بشيء من الأحياز والجهات . وإذا كان كذلك امتنع أن يكون المراد بقوله : « الرحمن على العرش استوى » : هو كونه مستقرا على العرش.
الثالث : أن ما قبل هذه الآية وما بعدها : مذكور لبيان كمال قدرة الله تعالى ، وغاية عظمته في الإلهية ، وكمال التصرف ، لأن قوله : « تنزيلا ممن خلق الأرض والسموات العلى » لا شك أن المفهوم منه : بيان كمال قدرة الله تعالى ، وكمال إلهيته . وقوله : « وله ما في السموات وما في الأرض وما بينهما وما تحت الثرى » بيان أيضا لكمال ملكه وإلهيته . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، وجب أن يكون قوله : ( الرحمن على العرش استوى ) كذلك وإلا لزم أن يكون ذلك كلاما أجنبيا عما قبله وعما بعده وذلك غير جائز . فأما إذا حملناه على كمال استيلائه على العرش ، الذي هو أعظم المخلوقات في الموجودات المحدثة ، كان ذلك موافقا لما قبل هذه الآية ولما بعدها . فكان هذا الوجه أولى .
الرابع: إن الجالس على العرش لابد وأن يكون الجزء الحاصل منه في يمين العرش ، غير الحاصل منه في يسار العرش : فيلزم كونه في نفسه مؤلفا ومركبا وذلك على الله تعالى محال .
The second type: that we speak about each of these aspects in detail:
As for that which they clung to first, and it is the six verses indicating Allah Almighty's istiwa' over the Throne. We say: It is not permissible that Allah Almighty intends by that istiwa' the meaning of physical settling (al-istiqrar) on the Throne. And this is indicated by aspects:
First: That which comes before this verse, which is His statement: 'A revelation from Him who created the earth and the highest heavens,' we have shown that this verse indicates that He, exalted, is not particularized by any of the spaces or directions.
Second: That which comes after this verse, which is His statement: 'To Him belongs whatever is in the heavens and whatever is in the earth,' we have shown that the heaven is that which has elevation and highness, so everything that is in a direction of above is a heaven. And if that is so, then His statement: 'To Him belongs whatever is in the heavens and whatever is in the earth' necessitates that everything occurring in a direction of above is in the heaven. And if that is so, then His statement: 'To Him belongs whatever is in the heavens and whatever is in the earth' necessitates that everything occurring in a direction of above is the property of Allah Almighty and possessed by Him. So if He, exalted, were particularized by a direction of above, it would necessitate His being possessed by Himself without a locus, and that is impossible. So it is established: that what comes before His statement 'The Most Merciful established over the Throne' and what comes after negate His, glorified and exalted, being particularized by any of the spaces and directions. And if that is so, it is impossible that what is intended by His statement 'The Most Merciful established over the Throne' is His being settled upon the Throne.
Third: That which comes before this verse and after it is mentioned to demonstrate the perfection of Allah Almighty's power, the utmost of His greatness in divinity, and the perfection of disposition, because His statement: 'A revelation from Him who created the earth and the highest heavens' — there is no doubt that the understood meaning from it is the demonstration of the perfection of Allah's power and the perfection of His divinity. And His statement: 'And to Him belongs whatever is in the heavens and whatever is in the earth and whatever is between them and whatever is under the soil' is also a demonstration of the perfection of His dominion and His divinity. And if the matter is so, it is necessary that His statement: 'The Most Merciful established over the Throne' also be such, otherwise that speech would be foreign to what is before it and what is after it, and that is not permissible. As for when we interpret it as the perfection of His domination over the Throne, which is the greatest of creations among originated beings, that would be consistent with what is before this verse and what is after it. So this aspect is more appropriate.
Fourth: The one sitting on the Throne necessarily has the part of him that is on the right side of the Throne not the same as the part of him on the left side of the Throne; so it necessitates that he is in himself composed and composite, and that is impossible with respect to Allah Almighty.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage presents the second approach of Imam Razi: a detailed refutation of the Karramiyya's proof from the six verses about istiwa'. He states that the intended meaning cannot be physical settling (istiqrar) on the Throne, and provides four proofs.
1. The first proof: The verse preceding the istiwa' verse (Q20:4) indicates that Allah is not confined to spaces or directions. Since He created the earth and high heavens, He is not limited by them.
2. The second proof: The verse following the istiwa' verse (Q20:6) says 'To Him belongs whatever is in the heavens and the earth.' Razi argues that 'heaven' refers to anything high, and everything in a high direction is in the heaven and belongs to Allah. If Allah were Himself in a high direction, He would be possessed by Himself (as part of His property), which is impossible. Therefore, the context negates direction.
3. The third proof: The surrounding verses speak of Allah's perfect power and divinity. The istiwa' verse must be interpreted in line with that theme. Interpreting istiwa' as domination (istila') over the Throne fits the context, while physical settling would be foreign to it.
4. The fourth proof: If someone sits on a throne, different parts of the body occupy different positions, implying composition and parts. This is impossible for Allah, who is not composed. Therefore, literal sitting is impossible. Each proof independently refutes the literal interpretation.

Key Terms
استيلاء
قدرة
إلهية
ملك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that literal interpretation is the only one that respects the text.
Correction: Razi shows that alternative interpretation (domination) is actually more consistent with the context and thus more respectful of the text's purpose.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, how does interpreting 'istawa' as domination (istila) fit the context better than literal sitting?
A) It makes the verse longer
B) It aligns with the surrounding verses about Allah's power and dominion
C) It is the only possible translation
D) It avoids using the word 'throne'

Key Takeaway
The third proof demonstrates that contextual coherence supports interpreting 'istawa' as complete domination rather than physical sitting.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you actively look at the verses before and after to understand the meaning, or do you often take verses out of context? How might this change your understanding of Allah's attributes?
?
If you truly believe that Allah's power is absolute and that every verse in the Quran is consistent with that, what would change in how you approach verses that seem to describe Allah in human terms? Are you willing to reinterpret them based on context, even if it challenges your initial reading?
?
Consider your own life: do you assess your beliefs and actions in light of the overall message of the Quran, or do you pick and choose verses that suit your desires? What would it mean for you to treat the Quran as a coherent whole, where every part reinforces the greatness of Allah?

Proof 4: Impossibility of Composition for the Divine
Razi's fourth proof from the impossibility of composition in the divine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why literal sitting on a throne would imply parts and composition, which is impossible for Allah.

Core Idea
Sitting requires a body with parts; Allah is not composed, so literal sitting is impossible.

Razi's fourth proof is a direct argument from the nature of sitting. If someone sits on a throne, different parts of their body occupy different positions. This implies the sitter has parts and is composed (mu'allaf wa murakkab). Since Allah is not composed, He cannot be literally sitting. This lesson examines that straightforward yet powerful argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the nature of sitting
Recognize that sitting on a physical object divides the body into parts on different sides (e.g., right and left).
2
Apply to Allah
Since Allah is not composed of parts, He cannot be literally sitting. The concept of sitting implies composition.
This proof is simple but profound.

Source Text

النوع الثاني : أن نتكلم عن كل واحد من هذه الوجوه على سبيل التفصيل :
أما الذي تمسكوا به أولا . وهو الآيات السنة الدالة على استواء الله تعالى على العرش. فنقول : إنه لا يجوز أن يكون مراد الله تعالى من ذلك الاستواء : هو الاستقرار على العرش . ويدل عليه وجوه :

Contextual Consistency of the Throne Verse
Imam Razi argues the throne verse must be interpreted consistently with surrounding verses about Allah's power and dominion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the surrounding verses determine the interpretation of the throne verse and why Imam Razi argues for metaphorical interpretation over literal.

Core Idea
A verse cannot be interpreted in isolation; its surrounding context dictates its meaning.

Imam Razi now presents a linguistic and contextual argument. He shows that the verses before and after Q. 20:5 all speak of Allah's absolute power and dominion. The verse about the Throne must harmonize with that theme, not contradict it. This is a powerful method of tafsir based on contextual consistency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to get the overall flow of the argument.
Notice that the argument is built on the immediate context of the verse.
2
Identify the surrounding verses
Razi refers to the verses before and after 'the throne verse'. Identify that these verses speak of Allah's creation and ownership of all things.
The specific references are not quoted, but the meaning is clear from the text.
3
Understand Razi's conclusion
Razi concludes that the throne verse must be interpreted in a way that is consistent with the theme of perfect power and dominion, not as a physical act.
This is the core of the contextual consistency argument.
4
Reflect on the principle
Ask yourself: Why is contextual consistency important in interpreting ambiguous verses? How does this principle safeguard divine transcendence?
This connects the lesson to broader Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : أن ما قبل هذه الآية وما بعدها مذكور لبيان كمال قدرة الله تعالى وغاية عظمته في الإلهية وكمال التصرف لأن قوله : تنزيلا ممن خلق الأرض والسموات العلى لا شك أن المفهوم منه بيان كمال قدرة الله تعالى وكمال إلهيته وقوله : وله ما في السموات وما في الأرض وما بينهما وما تحت الثرى بيان أيضا لكمال ملكه وإلهيته وإذا كان الأمر كذلك وجب أن يكون قوله : الرحمن على العرش استوى كذلك وإلا لزم أن يكون ذلك كلاما أجنبيا عما قبله وعما بعده وذلك غير جائز فأما إذا حملناه على كمال استيلائه على العرش الذي هو أعظم المخلوقات في الموجودات المحدثة كان ذلك موافقا لما قبل هذه الآية ولما بعدها فكان هذا الوجه أولى
Third: That what is before this verse and what is after it are mentioned to demonstrate the perfection of Allah's power, the utmost of His greatness in divinity, and the perfection of His disposal, because His saying: 'A revelation from Him who created the earth and the highest heavens' – undoubtedly the understood meaning from it is a statement of the perfection of Allah's power and the perfection of His divinity. And His saying: 'And to Him belongs whatever is in the heavens and whatever is on the earth and whatever is between them and whatever is under the ground' is also a statement of the perfection of His dominion and His divinity. And when the matter is thus, it is necessary that His saying: 'The Most Merciful istawa over the Throne' be likewise, otherwise it would be that it is foreign speech to what is before it and what is after it, and that is not permissible. So if we interpret it as the perfection of His domination over the Throne, which is the greatest of created things among contingent existents, that would be consistent with what is before this verse and what is after it. So this aspect is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument against a literal, spatial interpretation of istawa. Imam Razi uses contextual analysis: the verses before and after Qur'an 20:5 speak of Allah's absolute power and dominion. The verse in question must harmonize with them. If istawa were physical sitting, it would be an alien insertion. Instead, interpreting it as 'perfection of domination' (istila') maintains thematic unity. The author points to 'the Throne' as the greatest of creation, emphasizing Allah's absolute control over it, not physical placement.

استوى
استيلاء
عرش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The throne verse can be interpreted without considering its surrounding context.
Correction: The surrounding verses determine the meaning; istawa must be understood in light of them, consistent with Allah's power and dominion.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The throne verse must be interpreted consistently with the surrounding verses that speak of Allah's absolute power and dominion.

The Fourth Argument: Sitting Implies Composition
Imam Razi argues that sitting on a throne would necessitate physical parts, impossible for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's logical argument that Allah sitting on the Throne would necessitate physical parts, which is impossible for the simple essence of Allah.

Core Idea
Spatial relation entails parts, and Allah is beyond composition.

Imam Razi continues his series of rational arguments against anthropomorphism. In this fourth argument, he demonstrates that the very act of sitting on a throne implies spatial division, which forces composition on the sitter. Since Allah is absolutely simple, such an act is impossible. Let's unpack this concise yet powerful proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the logical flow: premise, inference, conclusion.
The argument is presented in a single sentence.
2
Identify the premise and inference
Identify the key components: what does sitting on a throne necessarily require? How does Imam Razi infer composition from that?
Look for the phrase 'فيلزم' indicating a necessary consequence.
3
Connect to theology
Reflect on why this argument is significant for affirming Allah's transcendence. How does it refute anthropomorphist interpretations of verses about the Throne?
This argument is part of a broader rebuttal of anthropomorphism.
4
Address a common misunderstanding
Some might argue that sitting does not imply composition if the sitter is non-physical. But Imam Razi's point is that any spatial relation between an entity and a physical object necessitates that the entity occupies space, which requires parts.
This helps solidify the logical necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: إن الجالس على العرش لابد وأن يكون الجزء الحاصل منه في يمين العرش غير الحاصل منه في يسار العرش فيلزم كونه في نفسه مؤلفا ومركبا وذلك على الله تعالى محال
Fourth: The one sitting on the throne must necessarily have the part of him that is on the right side of the throne different from the part of him that is on the left side of the throne. Thus it follows that he is in himself composed and compounded, and that is impossible for Allah, exalted.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This is a concise logical argument: sitting on a physical throne implies that different parts of the sitter occupy different spatial positions. This necessitates composition (tarkib) in the sitter. Since Allah is absolutely simple and non-composite (as established earlier in the book), such composition is impossible. The argument refutes any anthropomorphism that attributes a body to Allah.

Key Terms
جلس
تركيب
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sitting on the Throne does not imply composition if the sitter is non-physical or transcendent.
Correction: Imam Razi argues that any spatial relation between an entity and a physical object (the Throne) entails that the entity has parts corresponding to the spatial dimensions of the object. This is a logical necessity regardless of the nature of the entity.

Checkpoint

A) It is possible for Allah if He is not a body
B) It would require Allah to have parts, which is impossible
C) It is a metaphor for power
D) It only applies to created beings

Key Takeaway
The fourth argument demonstrates that literal sitting on the Throne is impossible because it entails composition, which contradicts Allah's absolute simplicity.

The Fifth Argument: Motion and Rest Entail Temporality
Razi presents a dilemma against literal sitting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma that refutes anthropomorphism and establishes Allah's transcendence beyond spatial properties.

Core Idea
If Allah could move or not, both options are impossible for the eternal.

Imam Razi now presents a razor-sharp argument that cuts through any literal interpretation of divine sitting. He constructs a dilemma: any being that occupies space either can move or cannot. Both horns lead to impossibilities when applied to Allah. This argument is a classic example of kalam reasoning—using logical contradictions to affirm transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the literal translation. Let the argument's force come through.
Notice the concise dilemma structure.
2
Identify the two horns
The passage presents two possibilities for a being that sits: capable of movement or not. Find each and see the conclusion drawn.
Both possibilities are eliminated.
3
Reflect on impossibility
Ask why each horn is impossible for Allah. The commentary will explain that temporality and deficiency contradict divine attributes.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : إن الجالس على العرش إن قدر على الحركة والانتقال كان محدثا لأن ما لا ينفك عن الحركة والسكون كان محدثا وإن لم يقدر على الحركة كان كالمربوط بل كان كالزمن بل أسوأ حالا منهما فإن الزمن إذا أراد الحركة في رأسه أو حدقتيه أمكنه ذلك وكذا المربوط وهو غير ممكن في الله تعالى
Fifth: The one sitting on the throne: if he is capable of movement and transition, then he is originated (muhdath), because whatever is not free from motion and rest is originated. And if he is not capable of movement, then he is like one tied up, rather like a cripple, or even worse than both. For the cripple, if he wants to move his head or his pupils, he can do so, and likewise the one tied up. But that is not possible for Allah, exalted.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This argument presents a dilemma: a being that sits either can move or cannot. If it can move, it is subject to motion and rest, which are accidents (a'rad). Anything that does not exist without accidents is itself temporal (hadith). Since Allah is eternal, this is impossible. If it cannot move, it is like a helpless captive, which is even more repugnant for the Omnipotent. The argument eliminates both possibilities, showing that sitting cannot be literal.

Key Terms
حركة
سكون
محدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Allah can sit on the throne without moving, or that sitting is compatible with His majesty.
Correction: Razi shows that any spatial placement entails either motion (temporality) or helplessness (deficiency), both impossible for the Eternal and Omnipotent.

Checkpoint
According to the fifth argument, what would it mean if Allah were incapable of movement while sitting?
A) It proves His eternity
B) He would be like a cripple or tied up, which is improper
C) He would be above motion
D) It shows His power over all things

Key Takeaway
Literal sitting implies either temporality or deficiency, both impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Razi says a cripple can at least move his head or eyes, but if Allah literally sits and cannot move, He would be worse off. What does this tell you about the danger of assigning physical attributes to Allah, even in good intention? Will you check your own descriptions of Allah today?

If you truly internalized that Allah is beyond all movement and rest, how would it change the way you rely on Him? Would you still think He 'comes down' or 'settles' in your mind during du'a?

The Sixth Argument: Spatial Location Implies Contamination or Limitation
Imam Razi presents a two-horned dilemma rejecting spatial location for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing spatial location to Allah leads to two absurd consequences, and how this argument reinforces divine transcendence.

Core Idea
Allah cannot be in a place because that would force either contamination or limitation.

Imam Razi presents a powerful dilemma. If Allah were literally inside the Throne, then either He would be present in all spaces (including filthy ones) or He would be confined to a limited region. Both options are utterly incompatible with His perfection. Let's unpack this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the structure 'لو حصل... فإن حصل... وإن لم يكن'.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The passage presents two conditionals: one if Allah is in all places, one if not. Find both and see how each leads to an impossibility.
The first horn leads to mixing with impurities; the second leads to having boundaries.
3
Trace each consequence
For each horn, ask: why is this consequence impossible for Allah? The first implies contamination; the second implies limitation and change.
Allah is pure and perfect, so both are impossible.
4
Connect to divine transcendence
Understand that this argument refutes the idea that Allah is literally in a physical location. It reinforces His absolute transcendence over creation.
This is a classic kalam argument against anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس : إنه لو حصل في العرش فإن حصل في سائر الأحياز يلزم منه كونه مخالطا للقاذورات والنجاسات وإن لم يكن كذلك كان له طرف ونهاية وزيادة ونقصان وكل ذلك على الله تعالى محال
Sixth: If He were located in the Throne, then if He were located in other spatial regions, it would entail His mixing with filth and impurities. And if not, then He would have a side and an end, and increase and decrease. And all of that is impossible for Allah, exalted.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
Razi presents a two-horned dilemma: if Allah occupies the Throne (a specific location), then either He also occupies all other spaces (which would mean He is present in filthy places, an absurdity) or He does not (which would mean He is limited to a finite region, having boundaries, edges, and thus being finite). Both are incompatible with Allah's absolute transcendence and perfection. Therefore, literal spatial occupancy is impossible.

Key Terms
حيّز
جهة
نهاية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that being in a specific place does not necessarily imply limitation or contamination.
Correction: This argument shows that spatial occupancy necessarily leads to either being present in all places (including impure ones) or being bounded. Both are impossible for Allah, so He transcends spatial location entirely.

Checkpoint

A) He would be subject to time and change
B) He would mix with impurities or have boundaries
C) He would become a body or a spirit
D) He would be seen or hidden

Key Takeaway
Allah is absolutely transcendent; attributing spatial location leads to absurd consequences that are incompatible with His perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Angels Carrying the Throne: Refuting Literalism
Imam Razi refutes literal interpretation using the verse about angels carrying the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses the verse about angels carrying the Throne to argue that Allah cannot be physically located on it, because that would entail creatures carrying the Creator.

Core Idea
If angels carry the Throne, Allah cannot be on it—the Creator carries, not is carried.

This lesson presents Imam Razi's seventh argument against anthropomorphism, based on the Qur'anic verse about angels bearing the Throne. Razi shows that interpreting the Throne as a literal seat leads to the absurd conclusion that angels would be carrying Allah. He then preempts a common objection and demonstrates that any literal interpretation collapses into either impossibility or abandonment of the apparent meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Notice the structure: Razi quotes the verse, draws an implication, and then addresses an objection.
2
Understand the core argument
Identify the key logical step: if the Throne is a place for Allah, then the angels carrying it would be carrying Allah. Razi calls this 'not reasonable' because the Creator cannot be carried by His creation.
3
Examine the objection and response
Razi anticipates the objection that Allah does not lean or depend on the Throne. He responds that 'settling' (istiqrar) inherently implies dependence; otherwise the term is meaningless. Study his analogy of a body on the ground.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
If one denies dependence, then the apparent meaning of settling is abandoned, and the verse loses its force as a proof for literalism. Razi thus shows that literal interpretation leads either to absurdity or loss of textual support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع : قوله تعالى : ويحمل عرش ربك فوقهم يومئذ ثمانية فلو كان العرش مكانا لمعبودهم لكانت الملائكة الذين يحملون العرش حاملين إله العالم وذلك غير معقول لأن الخالق هو الذي يحفظ المخلوق أما المخلوق فلا يحفظ الخالق ولا يحمله ولا يقال هذا إنما يلزم إذا كان الإله معتمدا على العرش متكئا عليه ونحن لا نقول ذلك لأنا نقول على هذا التقدير لا يكون الله تعالى مستقرا على العرش لأن الاستقرار على الشيء إنما يحصل إذا كان معتمدا عليه ألا ترى أنا إذا وضعنا جسما على الأرض قلنا إنه مستقر على الأرض ولا نقول الأرض مستقرة عليه وما ذاك إلا لأن الشيء معتمد على الأرض والأرض غير معتمدة عليه ولو لم يكن الإله معتمدا على العرش فحينئذ لا يكون مستقرا على العرش وعلى هذا التقدير يلزمهم ترك ظاهر الآية وحينئذ تخرج الآية عن كونها حجة
Seventh: Allah's saying: 'And the angels will bear your Lord's Throne above them on that Day, eight [angels]' – if the Throne were a place for their worshipped being, then the angels who carry the Throne would be carriers of the God of the universe. And that is not reasonable, because the Creator is the One who preserves the created being; as for the created being, it does not preserve the Creator nor carry Him. And it cannot be said: 'This only applies if the God is leaning on the Throne and reclining upon it, and we do not say that.' For we say: On this assumption, Allah would not be settled (mustaqirr) on the Throne, because settling on something only occurs if one is leaning upon it. Do you not see that when we place a body on the ground, we say it is settled on the ground, and we do not say the ground is settled upon it? That is only because the thing is leaning on the ground, and the ground is not leaning on it. And if the God were not leaning on the Throne, then He would not be settled on the Throne. On this assumption, they would be forced to abandon the apparent meaning of the verse, and thus the verse ceases to be a proof.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This is a detailed argument using Qur'an 69:17. If the Throne were Allah's seat, then angels carrying it would be carrying Allah—an absurdity since the Creator sustains all creation. Razi then preempts a potential objection: 'But we don't say He leans or reclines.' He responds that 'settling' (istiqrar) on something necessarily implies dependence on it; otherwise the term is meaningless. If one denies dependence, then the apparent meaning of 'istiqrar' is abandoned, and the verse cannot be used as proof for literal interpretation. Thus the literalist either falls into absurdity or loses textual support.

Key Terms
عرش
حمل
استقرار
اعتماد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that Allah can be on the Throne without depending on it; the term 'settling' does not require dependence.
Correction: Razi shows through the Arabic usage of 'istiqrar' and the analogy of a body on the ground that settling inherently implies leaning/dependence. Without dependence, the term loses its meaning, and the apparent meaning of the verse is abandoned.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the seventh argument regarding the angels carrying the Throne?
A) The Throne is a mighty creation, not a seat
B) If angels carry the Throne and Allah is on it, they would be carrying Allah, which is impossible
C) The angels are stronger than humans
D) The Throne will be destroyed on Judgment Day

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi argues that the verse about angels carrying the Throne cannot be taken literally because it would imply that created beings carry the Creator, which is impossible; any attempt to avoid this by denying dependence on the Throne abandons the apparent meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite verses about the Throne, do you mentally picture Allah as being 'above' or 'on' something? Razi's argument confronts you with the absurdity of such a picture. Are you willing to abandon that mental image, even if it feels less familiar? What would it mean for your worship to have no spatial direction when you pray?

Imam Razi begins an argument from Allah's existence before creation without place; the text cuts off.

Imam Razi presents the eighth argument for Allah's transcendence by pointing to His eternal existence before any created thing. Even though the text is cut short, the opening principles are clear and foundational. This lesson examines that opening and what it implies for divine transcendence.

Guided Path

2
Identify the key terms

Understand the logical structure

Imam Razi's Fifth Argument: Contingency or Impotence
Imam Razi presents the fifth argument using a disjunctive syllogism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi disproves a physical interpretation of Allah's sitting on the Throne using a disjunctive syllogism that leads to either contingency or impotence.

Core Idea
Sitting on a throne forces one to either move (contingent) or be immobile (powerless)—both impossible for Allah.

Imam Razi presents a powerful argument that cuts through the apparent metaphor. He shows that if Allah were literally seated on the Throne, He would either be capable of movement (making Him contingent) or incapable (making Him powerless). Both alternatives are absurd for the Creator, proving that istiwā' must be understood in a manner befitting His majesty. Let's examine this argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the argument's structure. Notice the disjunction introduced in the first sentence.
The argument is short but dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the two alternatives
The passage presents a clear either/or: the one sitting is either capable of movement or not. Pinpoint these two branches.
Look for the words 'إن قدر' and 'وإن لم يقدر'.
3
Analyze each alternative
For each alternative, see what consequence follows. The first leads to contingency (muḥdath), the second to being like a tied or paralyzed person—or worse.
Razi argues that even a paralyzed person can move his head/pupils, but the bound one cannot.
4
Understand the conclusion
Both alternatives are impossible for Allah, so the premise of a physical sitting must be false. This proves that istiwā' cannot be literal.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : إن الجالس على العرش إن قدر على الحركة والانتقال كان محدثاً . لأن مالا ينفك عن الحركة والسكون ، كان محدثا . وإن لم يقدر على الحركة . كان كالمربوط ، بل كان كالزمن ، بل أسوأ حالا منهما ، فإن الزمن إذا اراد الحركة فى رأسه أو حدقتيه ، أمكنه ذلك ، وكذا المربوط وهو غير ممكن فى الله تعالى .
The fifth: Indeed the one sitting on the throne, if he is capable of movement and transfer, then he is originated (muḥdath). Because whatever is not free from movement and stillness is originated. And if he is not capable of movement, then he is like one tied up, rather like a paralyzed person, and worse than both of them. For the paralyzed person, if he intends movement in his head or his pupils, that is possible for him; likewise the tied-up person. But that is impossible with respect to Allah, exalted.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth argument against the physicalist interpretation of istiwā' (Allah's settling on the Throne). Imam Razi uses a disjunctive syllogism: either the being seated on the Throne can move or cannot. If He can move and transfer, then He is subject to change and therefore contingent (muḥdath), because anything inseparable from movement and rest is contingent. If He cannot move, then He is like a bound or paralyzed person—or even worse—because a paralyzed person can still move his head or eyes, but the one on the throne would be completely immobile. Both alternatives are impossible for Allah, proving that a physical sitting is absurd.

Key Terms
العرش
الحركة
السكون
المحدث
المربوط
الزمن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The one seated on the Throne could be either capable or incapable of movement without contradiction.
Correction: Both alternatives lead to impossible consequences for Allah (contingency or impotence), so the premise of physical sitting is false.

Checkpoint
What does Imam Razi conclude if the one sitting on the throne cannot move?
A) He is eternal
B) He is like a paralyzed person
C) He is omnipotent
D) He is unaffected

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi's fifth argument shows that a literal sitting on the Throne forces an impossible choice between contingency and impotence, proving that Allah's istiwā' must be understood metaphorically.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Sixth Argument: Location Leads to Absurdity
Imam Razi presents a dilemma against spatial location for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's sixth argument, which demonstrates that the belief that Allah is located on the Throne necessarily leads to impossible consequences.

Core Idea
If Allah had a location, He would be either impure or limited—both impossible.

This short but powerful argument from Imam Razi is a classic example of the Kalam method of 'dilemma' (sabr wa-taqsim). He shows that any belief in a literal location for Allah leads to two equally impossible alternatives. By the end of this lesson, you will see why the attribute of spatial location cannot be affirmable of the Divine Essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the structure of the dilemma become clear.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
Notice the two conditions: 'if He were located in all spaces' and 'if that is not the case'. Each leads to an absurdity.
The first horn is about contamination, the second about limitation.
3
Understand why each horn is impossible
Mixing with filth contradicts divine purity. Having a boundary and being subject to increase/decrease contradicts divine perfection.
4
Internalize the conclusion
Imam Razi concludes 'All of that is impossible with respect to Allah.' This forces the rational thinker to reject any literal interpretation of 'istiwā'' or location.
This argument refutes anthropomorphism from a purely rational angle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس : إنه لو حصل فى العرش فإن حصل في سائر الأحياز يلزم منه كونه مخالطاً للقاذورات والنجاسات : وإن لم يكن كذلك، كان له طرف ونهاية وزيادة ونقصان ، وكل ذلك على الله تعالى محال .
The sixth: If He were located on the Throne, then if He were located in all other spaces, it would necessarily entail that He is mixing with filth and impurities. And if that is not the case, then He would have an edge and an end, and increase and decrease. All of that is impossible with respect to Allah, exalted.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This is the sixth argument. It presents another dilemma. If Allah is located on the Throne, one of two possibilities follows: either He also occupies all other spaces—since the universe contains impure places—which would require Him to mix with filth, which is absurd. Or He is not in all other spaces, but then He would be confined to a finite space with boundaries and dimensions, implying limitations and change, which are impossible for Allah. Thus, location is inconceivable for the Divine.

Key Terms
العرش
الأحياز
القاذورات
النجاسات
الطرف
النهاية
الزيادة
النقصان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that being in a specific place like the Throne does not necessarily imply contamination or limitation, or that 'on the Throne' is a metaphorical expression acceptable literally.
Correction: Imam Razi demonstrates that literal location, even on the Throne, logically forces either contamination (if everywhere) or limitation (if not everywhere). Both are impossible for Allah, so any literal spatial attribution must be rejected.

Checkpoint
According to the sixth argument, if Allah were on the throne but not in all spaces, what would necessarily follow?
A) He would be omnipresent
B) He would have boundaries and reduction
C) He would be pure
D) He would be eternal

Key Takeaway
Allah cannot be attributed with location because it would imply either contamination or limitation, both impossible for the Divine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray, do you ever unconsciously imagine Allah in a specific direction, like above the sky? How does this rational argument challenge that habit, and what can you do to remind yourself that Allah is beyond all spatial limitations?
?
This argument says Allah cannot be in a place because it would lead to either contamination or limitation. Does your heart fully accept that Allah is not confined to any location, even the highest heaven? If not, what does that reveal about your mental image of God?
?
If Allah's closeness is not physical but by knowledge and power, how should that change the way you seek nearness to Him? Are you satisfied with a God who is not 'close' in a spatial sense but is intimately aware of your every thought? How can you cultivate that awareness today?

The Seventh Argument: Angels Carrying the Throne Do Not Carry the Creator
Imam Razi refutes literalist interpretation of throne-carrying verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses the verse about angels carrying the Throne to refute the idea that the Throne is a place for Allah, thereby affirming divine transcendence.

Core Idea
If the Throne were Allah's place, angels would carry the Creator—an absurdity.

Imam Razi presents the seventh argument from the Quran, citing the verse that angels will carry the Throne. He argues that if the Throne were a literal place for Allah, then the angels would be carrying the Creator Himself, which is impossible because the Creator sustains all, not vice versa. He then addresses a potential objection and clarifies the concept of 'settling' (istiqrār), showing that the literalist interpretation leads to abandonment of the apparent meaning of the verse. Let's examine this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and initial argument
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Imam Razi cites Quran 69:17 and draws a conditional implication.
The verse is about the Day of Judgment, but Razi uses it to discuss divine transcendence.
2
Understand the absurd consequence
If the Throne were a place for Allah, then the angels carrying the Throne would be carrying the Creator. Razi says this is inconceivable because the Creator preserves all, not the other way around.
This is the core of the reductio ad absurdum.
3
Consider the opponent's objection
The opponent might say that they do not claim Allah is supported on the Throne, so being carried does not apply.
Razi anticipates this objection to strengthen his argument.
4
Follow Razi's response about 'settling'
Razi argues that 'settling' (istiqrār) on something requires being supported by it, as in the example of a body on the ground. If Allah is not supported on the Throne, He cannot be settled on it.
This undermines the literalist interpretation of istiwā' (establishment) as well.
5
See how the verse ceases to be a proof
If the opponent abandons the apparent meaning of 'settling', then the verse cannot be used as evidence for physical location. The argument refutes itself.
Razi concludes that the literalist reading defeats its own purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع : قوله تعالى : ويحمل عرش ربك فوقهم يومئذ ثمانية ، فلو كان العرش مكاناً لمعبودهم ، لكانت الملائكة الذين يحملون العرش حاملين إله العالم . وذلك غير معقول ، لأن الخالق هو الذي يحفظ المخلوق. أما المخلوق فلا يحفظ الخالق ولا يحمله. ولا يقال : هذا إنما يلزم إذا كان الإله معتمداً على العرش متكئاً عليه ، ونحن لا نقول ذلك . لأنا نقول على هذا التقدير : لا يكون الله تعالى مستقراً على العرش، لأن الاستقرار على الشيء ، إنما يحصل إذا كان معتمداً عليه ألا ترى أنا إذا وضعنا جسما على الأرض ، قلنا : إنه مستقر على الأرض ، ولا نقول : الأرض مستقرة عليه. وماذاك إلا لأن الشيء معتمدا على الأرض ، والأرض غير معتمدة عليه ، ولو لم يكن الإله معتمداً على العرش ، فحينئذ لا يكون مستقراً على العرش ، وعلى هذا التقدير ، يلزمهم ترك ظاهر الآية . وحينئذ تخرج الآية عن كونها حجة
The seventh: The saying of the Most High: 'And eight will bear the Throne of your Lord above them on that day.' If the Throne were a place for their worshipped being, the angels who bear the Throne would be bearers of the God of the worlds. That is inconceivable, because the Creator is the One who preserves the created being. As for the created being, he does not preserve the Creator nor carry Him. And it cannot be said: this only follows if the god is supported on the Throne, leaning upon it, and we do not say that. For we say on this estimation: Allah, exalted, would not be settled on the Throne, because settling on something only occurs if it is supported upon it. Do you not see that if we place a body on the ground, we say it is settled on the ground, and we do not say the ground is settled upon it. That is only because the thing is supported on the ground, and the ground is not supported upon it. And if the god is not supported on the Throne, then He is not settled on the Throne. On this estimation, they are compelled to abandon the apparent meaning of the verse. And then the verse ceases to be a proof.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This is the seventh argument, a scriptural reasoning based on the verse about angels carrying the Throne (Quran 69:17). If the Throne were a literal place for Allah, then the angels carrying the Throne would be carrying the Creator. That is absurd because the Creator sustains the creation, not vice versa. The opponent might object that they do not claim Allah is supported on the Throne. The Imam responds that if Allah is not supported on it, then He is not settled on it, because 'settling' (istiqrār) implies dependence. The popular example: a body placed on the ground is said to be settled on the ground, not the ground on it, because the body depends on the ground. If dependence is denied, then the literal meaning of 'settling' is lost, and the verse cannot be used as proof for physical settlement. Thus, the literalist interpretation defeats itself.

Key Terms
العرش
الملائكة
الحمل
الاستقرار
الاعتماد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe the verse about angels carrying the Throne proves that Allah is physically located on the Throne.
Correction: Imam Razi shows that if that were true, the angels would be carrying the Creator, which is absurd. The verse actually supports divine transcendence.

Checkpoint
What does Imam Razi say would follow if the Throne were a literal place for Allah?
A) The angels would be carrying the Creator
B) The Throne would be independent
C) Allah would be dependent on angels
D) The angels would be divine

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi's argument shows that the verse about angels carrying the Throne refutes the notion of spatial location for Allah, affirming His transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself imagining Allah as 'up there' or sitting on a throne? How does this argument challenge that inner picture, and what will you do to replace it with a proper understanding of transcendence?
?
Imam Razi shows that if we interpret the verse literally, we end up with an absurdity. What other Islamic beliefs do you hold that might be based on literal readings without thinking through the logical consequences? Are you willing to scrutinize them?
?
The angels carry the Throne, but cannot carry the Creator. What does this teach you about your own relationship with Allah? Do you ever act as if you can 'carry' or benefit Allah by your worship, or do you truly recognize that He is completely independent?

The Eighth Argument: The Implication of 'Thumma'
Imam Razi argues that since Allah existed without the Throne, He cannot become settled on it later.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses the word 'thumma' (then) in the Quranic verse to argue that Allah's istiwā' over the Throne cannot be a literal physical settlement.

Core Idea
Temporal delay implies change, and change cannot apply to the Eternal.

Imam Razi presents the eighth argument against anthropomorphism by analyzing the Quranic word 'thumma'. He shows that the verse's own wording indicates a temporal sequence, which would require change in Allah if taken literally. This lesson walks through his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the argument.
Notice the concise structure: premise, impossibility claim, Quranic evidence.
2
Understand the premise
The argument begins by stating that Allah existed eternally without any Throne or place. This is a key foundation.
This establishes that Allah's existence is prior to all creation, including the Throne.
3
Analyze the role of 'thumma'
Imam Razi cites the verse 'Then He istawā over the Throne' and notes that 'thumma' indicates delay (tarākhī). Consider what this delay implies about the nature of istiwā'.
Delay suggests that istiwā' happened after creation, implying a change in Allah if taken literally.
4
Reach the conclusion
If Allah were eternally settled on the Throne, there would be no need for the word 'thumma'. Therefore, the literalist interpretation is inconsistent with the wording of the verse.
The argument shows that the plain meaning of the text contradicts the anthropomorphic claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثامن : إنه تعالى كان ولا عرش ولا مكان. ولما خلق الخلق ، يستحيل أن يقال : إنه تعالى صار مستقراً على العرش ، بعد أن لم يكن كذلك . لأنه تعالى قال : ثم استوى على العرش ، وكلمة ، ثم ، للتراخي .
The eighth: Indeed He, exalted, existed while there was no Throne and no place. And when He created the creation, it is impossible to say that He, exalted, became settled on the Throne after having not been so. Because He, exalted, said: 'Then He istawā over the Throne', and the word 'thumma' indicates delay.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This is the eighth argument, using the temporal sequence implied by the word 'thumma' (then) in the Quranic verse. God existed eternally without any Throne or place. After creating the creation, it is inconceivable that He would change by acquiring settlement on the Throne, because that would imply He was previously lacking an attribute, which is a change in the eternal. The verse states 'thumma istawā', and the word 'thumma' indicates temporal delay. This shows that the 'istiwā' occurred after the creation of the heavens and earth, which is a temporal event. But if God were eternally on the Throne, there would be no need for delay. Therefore, the literalist interpretation is inconsistent with the verse's wording.

Key Terms
العرش
المكان
الاستقرار
ثم
التراخي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: 'thumma' in the verse simply indicates sequence without implying any change in Allah.
Correction: Imam Razi argues that 'thumma' indicates temporal delay (tarākhī), which would mean Allah acquired the attribute of istiwā' after not having it, implying change - impossible for the Eternal.

Checkpoint
What does the word 'thumma' indicate according to Imam Razi?
A) Immediate succession
B) Delay
C) Simultaneity
D) Causality

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi's eighth argument uses the linguistic implication of 'thumma' (then) to show that a literal interpretation of istiwā' would entail change in Allah, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you believed that Allah acquired a new relationship with the Throne after creation, what would that imply about His perfection and self-sufficiency? How does this lesson compel you to reaffirm that Allah is unchanged by His creation?
?
The word 'thumma'—a small detail—carries such weight in defending tawhid. Are there other seemingly minor words or phrases in the Quran that you have glossed over without deep reflection? Will you commit to studying the Quran with greater attention to its linguistic precision from now on?

The Ninth Argument: Verses of Divine Presence
Imam Razi uses three Quranic verses to argue against literal confinement to the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses Quranic verses about Allah's closeness and presence to argue against His confinement to the Throne.

Core Idea
Clear verses of divine presence challenge literal confinement to the Throne.

Imam Razi continues to dismantle literalist interpretations by presenting more Quranic evidence. The argument attributed to Al-Qāsim cites three verses that speak of Allah's closeness and omnipresence, which directly contradict the idea that He is fixed on the Throne. This lesson examines how these verses are used as a hermeneutical counterweight to the throne verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, noticing the three verses cited and the concluding principle.
The style is compact; each verse is referenced by its opening words.
2
Identify the three verses
Find the references: 'We are closer than the jugular vein', 'He is with you wherever you are', and 'He is God in heaven and God on earth'.
These are all verses that imply a universal divine presence.
3
Understand the argument's structure
Note that the argument first states that these verses negate literal settlement on the Throne, then asserts that interpreting the throne verses in light of these is equally valid as the reverse.
This is a standard principle of tafsir: general verses clarify specific ones.
4
Reflect on the hermeneutical principle
Consider why the argument says interpreting these verses to negate the apparent meaning of throne verses is 'not more warranted than the opposite'.
It undercuts the opponent's claim that their interpretation is the only valid one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القاسم : إن ظاهر قوله تعالى: ونحن أقرب إليه من حبل الوريد وقوله: وهو معكم أينما كنتم، وقوله: وهو الذي في السماء إله وفي الأرض إله، ينفي كونه مستقراً على العرش، وليس تأويل هذه الآيات لنفي الآيات التي تمسكوا بها على ظاهرها: أولى من العكس
Al-Qāsim: Indeed the apparent meaning of His saying: 'And We are closer to him than the jugular vein' and His saying: 'And He is with you wherever you are' and His saying: 'And it is He who is God in heaven and God on earth' negates His being settled on the Throne. And interpreting these verses to negate the verses they adhere to in their apparent meaning is not more warranted than the opposite.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents an argument attributed to 'Al-Qāsim' (possibly a scholar or a reference). It points out that other Quranic verses clearly indicate that Allah is not confined to a specific place. The verse 'We are closer to him than the jugular vein' (Qaf 16) and 'He is with you wherever you are' (Al-Hadid 4) and 'He is God in heaven and God on earth' (Az-Zukhruf 84) all imply a universal presence that contradicts the idea of being localized on a throne. The argument then states that interpreting these verses to negate the apparent meaning of the throne verses is not more valid than the reverse—i.e., interpreting the throne verses in light of these clear verses. This is a standard hermeneutical principle: general or unambiguous verses take precedence over particular or ambiguous ones.

Key Terms
العرش
الاستقرار
الحبل الوريد
المعية
التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the throne verses are the only clear verses about Allah's location, ignoring verses of divine presence.
Correction: Imam Razi shows that verses like 'He is with you' are equally clear and challenge a literal confinement to the Throne.

Checkpoint

A) More warranted
B) Not more valid than the opposite
C) The only valid method
D) Forbidden

Key Takeaway
Clear Quranic verses about Allah's presence and closeness, if taken literally, negate His confinement to the Throne just as the throne verses would require interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The argument shows that even long-held assumptions about Allah must be tested against the Qur'an. Is there a belief about Allah you hold that you have never examined? Are you willing to submit it to the Qur'an today, even if it shatters your comfort?

The Tenth Argument: Istiwā' Means Domination
Imam Razi concludes that istiwā' means domination via rational and linguistic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi combines rational proofs and linguistic usage to conclude that istiwā' (Allah's establishment over the Throne) means domination and management, not physical sitting.

Core Idea
Istiwā' means Allah's absolute dominion, not physical settlement.

In this concluding argument, Imam Razi brings together the decisive rational proofs and the linguistic conventions of Arabic to show that the term 'istiwā' in the Quranic verse 'al-Rahmānu ‘alā al-‘Arshi istawā' cannot mean physical sitting or settlement. Instead, it must mean Allah's complete domination, subjugation, and management of the universe. This argument synthesizes reason and language to affirm divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice how Imam Razi structures his argument from rational premise to linguistic evidence.
The passage is the tenth argument in the series.
2
Understand the rational premise
Imam Razi begins by recalling that rational proofs have shown Allah is not confined to any direction. This is the foundational premise that rules out physical settlement.
This is a key point to grasp.
3
Observe the linguistic evidence
Next, see how he uses a line of poetry and Quranic examples to show that the Arabic language allows istiwā' to mean domination, and that God's actions are described in a way consistent with custom.
The verse 'And Allah mocks them' is a clear example of figurative language.
4
Apply the analogy
Finally, consider the analogy with the word 'qiyām' which shifts from literal standing to undertaking a task. This reinforces the point that words can have multiple meanings.
This analogy helps solidify the interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العاشر : إن الدلائل العقلية القاطعة التي قدمنا ذكرها ، تبطل كون الله تعالى مختصا بشيء من الجهات . وإذا ثبت هذا، ظهر أنه ليس المراد من الاستواء : الاستقرار . فوجب أن يكون المراد : هو الاستيلاء ، والقهر ونفاذ القدر ، وجريان الأحكام الإلهية . وهذا مستقيم على قانون اللغة. فقد قال الشاعر : قد استوى بشر على العراق من غير سيف ودم مهراق والذي يقرر ذلك: أن الله تعالى إنما أنزل القرآن بحسب عرف أهل اللسان وعاداتهم . ألا ترى أنه تعالى قال: وهو خادعهم وقال: وهو أهون عليه وقال: ومكروا ومكر الله وقال: الله يستهزئ بهم، والمراد في الكل : أنه تعالى يعاملهم معاملة الخادعين والماكرين والمستهزئين . فهكذا ههنا ، المراد من الاستواء على العرش : التدبير بأمر الملك والملكوت . ونظيره : أن القيام أصله الانتصاب ، ثم يذكر بمعنى الشروع في الأمر ، كما يقال : قام بالملك.
The tenth: Indeed the definitive rational proofs we have previously mentioned invalidate that Allah, exalted, is particularized with any direction. When this is established, it becomes clear that what is meant by istiwā' is not settlement (istiqrār). So it must be that what is meant is domination (istīlā'), and subjugation (qahr), and penetration of decree, and execution of divine rulings. And this is consistent with the rule of language. For the poet said: 'Bishr istawā over Iraq without sword and bloodshed.' And what establishes that is that Allah, exalted, revealed the Qur'an according to the custom of the people of the language and their habits. Do you not see that He, exalted, said: 'And He is making them mock' and said: 'And it is easier for Him' and said: 'And they plotted and Allah plotted' and said: 'Allah mocks them' and the meaning in all is that He, exalted, deals with them in the manner of those who mock, scheme, and deride. So similarly here, what is meant by istiwā' over the Throne is the management of the domain of kingship and sovereignty. And an analogy for that is that 'standing' (qiyām) originally means uprightness, then it is used with the meaning of beginning a matter, as it is said: 'He stood (qāma) with the rule.'
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This final argument synthesizes the rational and linguistic evidence. Imam Razi begins with the rational proofs established earlier (presumably referring to previous arguments) that Allah cannot be confined to a direction. Since the rational proofs are decisive, the term 'istiwā' cannot mean physical settlement. The only remaining meaning consistent with revelation and reason is 'domination' (istīlā'), 'subjugation' (qahr), and the execution of divine decrees. He then supports this with linguistic evidence: Arabic idiom permits istiwā' to mean 'conquer' or 'dominate', as in the poetic line about Bishr dominating Iraq without violence. Moreover, the Qur'an itself uses figurative language for God in many places, e.g., 'Allah mocks them', 'Allah plots', where the literal meaning is not intended but rather a comparative meaning. This shows that the Qur'an follows the Arabic custom of using words metaphorically. Therefore, istiwā' over the Throne means God's management of the universe as King. He further gives an analogy: the word 'qiyām' literally means standing, but can mean undertaking an action, e.g., 'he stood with the rule' meaning he undertook the management.

Key Terms
الاستواء
الاستيلاء
القهر
التدبير
الجهات
القانون اللغة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Istiwā' must be interpreted literally as physical sitting.
Correction: Imam Razi demonstrates that both rational proofs and linguistic usage show that istiwā' means domination and management, not physical settlement.

Checkpoint
What does Imam Razi conclude is the meaning of istiwā' in the verse?
A) Physical sitting
B) Settlement
C) Domination and management
D) Physical elevation

Key Takeaway
The definitive rational proofs along with Arabic linguistic conventions establish that istiwā' over the Throne means Allah's absolute domination and management, not physical sitting.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the verse about Allah's istiwā' over the Throne, do you deeply feel that He is in control of every detail of your life, or do you fall into picturing Him in a certain direction? How can you train your heart to submit to His absolute dominion without limitation?
?
Imam Razi used rational proofs to strip away any physical attributes from Allah. Have you ever allowed your mind to imagine Allah in a finite way? After this lesson, will you actively reject such thoughts and affirm His transcendence even when your heart struggles?
?
The Qur'an uses figurative language to describe Allah's actions. When you read verses like 'Allah mocks them', do you pause to understand the intended meaning, or do you let your imagination run? Commit to learning the correct interpretation as a matter of faith.

Refuting the Literalist Claim from 'Thumma'
Razi presents and refutes the literalist argument from the word 'thumma'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi refutes the literalist argument that the word 'thumma' implies a temporal sequence for Allah's istawa.

Core Idea
The word 'thumma' does not force a literal reading when other verses negate location.

Imam Razi addresses a key objection from literalists: the word 'thumma' (then) in the verse 'thumma stawa' seems to indicate a sequence, implying Allah became settled after not being. But Razi shows that this argument can be countered by other Quranic verses that deny any specific location for Allah. In this lesson, we examine this refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and translation of the opponent's argument and Razi's response.
2
Identify the opponent's reasoning
Notice how the literalists use 'thumma' to claim a temporal change in Allah's state.
3
Understand Razi's counter
He cites three verses that negate any specific location for Allah and argues for equal validity of figurative interpretation.
The verses: 'We are nearer than the jugular vein', 'He is with you wherever you are', 'He is Allah in the heavens and on earth'.
4
Reflect on the logical principle
Why is it not more appropriate to interpret one set of verses literally over the other?
This demonstrates the principle of mutual refutation in tafsir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن يقال : إنه تعالى صار مستقراً على العرش ، بعد أن لم يكن كذلك . لأنه تعالى قال : ثم استوى ، على العرش ، وكلمة ، ثم ، للتراخي . القاسم : إن ظاهر قوله تعالى: ونحن أقرب إليه من حبل الوريد وقوله : وهو معكم أينما كنتم ، وقوله : « وهو الذي في السماء إله، وفي الأرض إله ، ينفى كونه مستقراً على العرش ، وليس تأويل هذه الآيات لنفى الآيات التي تمسكوا بها على ظاهرها : أولى من العكس . العاشر : إن الدلائل العقلية القاطعة التى قدمنا ذكرها ، تبطل كونه تعالى مختصا بشيء من الجهات . وإذا ثبت هذا، ظهر أنه ليس المراد من الاستواء : الاستقرار . فوجب أن يكون المراد : هو الاستيلاء ، والقهر ونفاذ القدر ، وجريان الأحكام الإلهية . وهذا مستقيم على قانون اللغة. فقد قال الشاعر : قد استوى بشر على العراق من غير سيف ودم مهراق والذي يقرر ذلك: أن الله تعالى إنما أنزل القرآن بحسب عرف أهل اللسان وعاداتهم . ألا ترى أنه تعالى قال: وهو خادعهم وقال: وهو أهون عليه وقال : ومكروا ومكر الله ، وقال : « الله يستهزئ بهم ، والمراد فى الكل : أنه تعالى يعاملهم معاملة الخادعين والماكرين والمستهزئين . فكذا ههنا ، المراد من الاستواء على العرش : التدبير بأمر الملك والملكوت . ونظيره : أن القيام أصله الانتصاب ، ثم يذكر بمعنى الشروع في الأمر ، كما يقال : قام بالملك.
It may be said: He, exalted, became settled on the Throne after not being so, because He, exalted, said: 'Then He established Himself (istawa) over the Throne,' and the word 'then' indicates delay. Al-Qasim: The apparent meaning of His statement, exalted: 'And We are nearer to him than the jugular vein,' and His statement: 'And He is with you wherever you are,' and His statement: 'And He is Allah in the heavens and Allah on earth,' negates His being settled on the Throne, and interpreting these verses to negate the verses they hold to according to their apparent meaning is not more appropriate than the opposite. Tenth: The definitive rational proofs that we have mentioned refute that He, exalted, is particular to any direction. When this is established, it becomes clear that what is meant by 'istawa' is not settlement. So it is necessary that what is meant is domination (istila'), subjugation, the execution of power, and the flow of divine decrees. This is consistent with the law of language. For the poet said: 'Bishr has taken control (istawa) of Iraq without sword or spilled blood.' And what establishes this is that Allah, exalted, only revealed the Quran according to the custom of the people of the language and their habits. Do you not see that He, exalted, said: 'And He deceives them' and said: 'And it is easy for Him' and said: 'And they plotted and Allah plotted' and said: 'Allah mocks them,' and the meaning in all is that He, exalted, treats them with the treatment of deceivers, plotters, and mockers. Similarly here, what is meant by 'istawa over the Throne' is the management of the kingdom and dominion. Its analogy is that 'qiyam' originally means standing upright, then it is used in the sense of undertaking a matter, as is said: 'He undertook (qama) the rule.'
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a combined refutation of the literalist claim that 'istawa' means physical settlement and a positive proof that it means domination. The structure begins by presenting the opponent's argument: the verse 'thumma stawa' with 'thumma' (then) implying a temporal sequence, so Allah became settled on the Throne after not being so. Then comes the response: first, other verses such as 'We are nearer than the jugular vein' and 'He is with you wherever you are' and 'He is Allah in the heavens and on earth' negate any specific location. If the literalists interpret these verses figuratively to avoid contradicting their literal reading of 'istawa', the opposite interpretation (taking 'istawa' figuratively) is equally valid. Thus no preference. Second, Razi presents the tenth rational proof: the definitive rational proofs already given show Allah is not confined to any direction. Therefore 'istawa' cannot mean physical settlement; it must mean domination (istila'), subjugation, and execution of power. This is linguistically sound, as exemplified by the poet saying 'Bishr has taken control of Iraq without sword or spilled blood', where 'istawa' clearly means domination. Razi then argues that the Quran is revealed in the customary language of the Arabs, who use verbs of human action for God in a figurative sense, as in 'deceives', 'plots', 'mocks' — where the real meaning is that God treats them as such. So here 'istawa' means management of the kingdom. The analogy of 'qiyam' (standing) is given: it originally means physical standing, but is used to mean 'undertaking' a task, as in 'he undertook the rule' (qama bil-mulk). This supports the figurative interpretation.

Key Terms
ثم
استوى
الاستقرار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'thumma' must indicate a temporal sequence for Allah's action, implying a change in His essence.
Correction: Razi responds by citing other verses that show Allah is not confined to a location, making the literal interpretation problematic. The presence of 'thumma' does not compel a temporal reading when other scriptural evidence points to transcendence.

Checkpoint
Which of the following verses does Razi use to counter the literalist claim that 'istawa' means physical settlement based on 'thumma'?
A) 'He is with you wherever you are'
B) 'And We are nearer to him than the jugular vein'
C) 'He is Allah in the heavens and on earth'
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The presence of 'thumma' does not compel a literal reading when other scriptural and rational evidence points to Allah's transcendence above location.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever insisted on a literal interpretation of a verse without considering other clear evidence from the Quran or reason, simply because it seemed obvious? How might that have led you to a misunderstanding of Allah's attributes?
?
When you read the verse 'thumma stawa 'ala al-arsh', do you find yourself tempted to imagine Allah physically moving or settling? What does that reveal about your own tendency to anthropomorphize the Divine, and how can you guard against it?
?
Razi shows that we must weigh all evidence together rather than clinging to one text. In your own spiritual journey, are there areas where you favor one proof while ignoring others that clearly contradict your interpretation? Will you commit today to seeking a holistic understanding of Allah's revelation?

Rational and Linguistic Proofs for Istawa as Domination
Razi presents the rational proof that Allah is not confined to direction, then supports the interpretation of istawa as domination with linguistic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the tenth rational proof and the linguistic evidence that 'istawa' means domination (istila), not physical settlement.

Core Idea
Rational proofs negate direction; language confirms 'istawa' means control, not settlement.

After refuting the literalist objection from 'thumma', Imam Razi now presents the definitive rational proof: since Allah cannot be confined to any direction, 'istawa' cannot mean physical settlement. He then provides linguistic support from poetry and Quranic usage, showing that 'istawa' is used figuratively for domination, just as other verbs are used figuratively for Allah. This lesson explains these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the rational proof and linguistic arguments.
2
Grasp the rational proof
Understand why the proof that Allah is not in a direction leads to the conclusion that istawa means domination.
This is the tenth rational proof, building on earlier ones.
3
Examine the linguistic evidence
Look at the poet's line 'Bishr has taken control of Iraq' and the Quranic examples of figurative usage (deception, plotting, mocking).
4
Reflect on the analogy of 'qiyam'
Consider how 'qiyam' shifts from physical standing to undertaking a task, similar to 'istawa' shifting to domination.
This reinforces the legitimate figurative interpretation.
