First Branch: No Substitution of Ambiguous Terms
Imam Razi states the first branch: forbidding substitution of ambiguous terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rationale behind the Salaf's prohibition against substituting ambiguous divine attributes with other ambiguous terms.

Core Idea
Even ambiguous terms differ in how much they suggest falsehood; changing them risks greater misguidance.

Imam al-Razi begins the first methodological branch: the prohibition of substituting one ambiguous term with another. He provides a rational argument based on the danger of increasing false suggestion and supports it with a legal analogy. This lesson explains the reasoning and its application to divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation to get the overall meaning.
Notice the precise language used for prohibition and precaution.
2
Identify the core ruling
Find the sentence stating the ruling: it is not permissible to replace one ambiguous word with another. This is the first branch.
The ruling applies whether the replacement is Arabic or Persian.
3
Understand the reason
Imam al-Razi gives the reason: some ambiguous terms are more suggestive of falsehood than others, and increasing false suggestion without need is prohibited.
Consider why even a slight increase in false suggestion matters when speaking about Allah.
4
Examine the analogy
He draws an analogy to the Islamic law of 'iddah, where precaution is applied broadly to avoid harming lineage rulings.
Note that caution in matters of Allah's attributes is even more important.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that if precaution is taken in worldly matters, it is more fitting to do so in theology.
This highlights the Salaf's cautionary approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول : إنه لا يجوز تبديل لفظ من الألفاظ المتشابهة ، بلفظ آخر متشابه ، سواء كان بالعربية أو بالفارسية . وذلك لأن الألفاظ المتشابهة قد يكون بعضها أكثر إيهاما للباطل من البعض . والزيادة في الإيهام من غير حاجة إليها لا يجوز . بلى . قد تكون زيادة الإبهام حاصلة في اللفظين إلا أن التمييز بين هذا القسم، والقسم الأول فيه عسر . فالاحتياط : الامتناع من الكل . ألا ترى أن الشرع أوجب العدة على الموطوءة ، لبراءة الرحم، احتياطا لحكم النسب ، ثم قالوا : تجب العدة على العقيم، والآيسة ، وعند العزل . لأن بواطن الأرحام، لا يعلمها إلا علام الغيوب ؟ فإيجاب العدة أهون من ركوب الخطر . إلا أن الخطر في معرفة ذات الله تعالى وصفاته ، أعظم من الخطر في العدة . فإذا راعينا الاحتياط به، فلأن نراعيه ههنا أولى .
First: It is not permissible to replace one ambiguous word with another ambiguous word, whether in Arabic or Persian. That is because ambiguous words may be more suggestive of falsehood than others. And increasing suggestion (of falsehood) without need is not permissible. Rather, it may be that increased ambiguity occurs in both words, but distinguishing between this category and the first category is difficult. So caution dictates abstaining from all. Do you not see that the Law obligated the waiting period ('iddah) on the woman who has been sexually penetrated, to ensure the womb's emptiness, as a precaution for the ruling of lineage, and then they said: The 'iddah is obligatory on the barren woman, the post-menopausal woman, and in case of coitus interruptus, because the interiors of wombs none knows them except the Knower of the unseen? So imposing the 'iddah is easier than risking danger. Yet the danger in knowing the Essence of God Almighty and His attributes is greater than the danger in the 'iddah. If we accordingly observe precaution regarding it, then it is more fitting that we observe it here.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage presents the first branch of the Salaf's methodology: the prohibition of substituting one ambiguous (mutashābih) term with another ambiguous term. Imam al-Razi begins by stating the ruling: it is not allowed to replace one ambiguous expression with another, regardless of language (Arabic or Persian). The reason is that some ambiguous terms are more suggestive (īhām) of false meaning than others. Increasing such suggestion without necessity is impermissible. He acknowledges that sometimes both terms have equal ambiguity, but distinguishing between cases of equal and unequal ambiguity is difficult, so the precautionary principle (iḥtiyāṭ) demands abstaining from all substitution. He then draws an analogy from Islamic law: the 'iddah (waiting period) is required for a woman after intercourse to ensure the womb is empty, as a precaution for lineage rulings. This precaution is applied even to women who cannot possibly be pregnant (barren, post-menopausal, or after coitus interruptus) because only God knows the hidden state of wombs. If such precaution is taken in worldly matters, then it is even more necessary in matters of God's essence and attributes, where the risk is far greater. Thus, the first branch forbids any substitution of ambiguous terms to avoid even potential misguidance.

Key Terms
تبديل
الألفاظ المتشابهة
إيهام
احتياط
العدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Substituting an ambiguous term with another is harmless if both are ambiguous.
Correction: Imam al-Razi argues that ambiguous terms differ in degree of false suggestion, so substitution may increase falsehood without need; therefore it is prohibited.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi, why is it impermissible to substitute one ambiguous divine attribute expression with another?
A) Because the original term is always clearer.
B) Because ambiguous terms may differ in degree of suggesting falsehood, and increasing that without need is prohibited.
C) Because substitution is only allowed in Persian.
D) Because the Salaf never used ambiguous terms.

Key Takeaway
The Salaf prohibited substituting ambiguous terms because even slight increases in false suggestion are dangerous when speaking about Allah, and precaution (ihtiyat) demands avoiding all unnecessary substitution.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Imam al-Razi argues that precaution in matters of Allah's essence is even more important than precaution in lineage. Is your concern for protecting your and others' understanding of Allah's attributes as intense as your concern for preserving worldly matters like family ties or reputation? What is one area of your faith where you have been lax in 'ihtiyat'?
?
The Salaf refrained from even substituting one ambiguous word for another out of fear of misguidance. But have you ever found yourself preferring a particular theological wording because it sounds more sophisticated or persuasive, even if it might not be from the Salaf's methodology? Second Branch: Avoiding Derived Forms of Ambiguous Terms
Imam Razi explains why derived verbal forms of ambiguous terms are prohibited.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Razi prohibits deriving active participles from ambiguous divine attributes like 'istawā' and the linguistic principle behind it.

Core Idea
The active participle implies settledness, so we avoid it for God.

Imam al-Razi continues his method of safeguarding divine transcendence by laying down a second rule: we must avoid deriving active participle forms from ambiguous terms used for God. This lesson explains the linguistic reason from the science of rhetoric and a supporting Qur'anic parallel.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the ruling and the reasoning Imam Razi provides.
Pay attention to the parallel he draws from the teaching verses.
2
Understand the linguistic principle
Imam Razi states that in ʿilm al-bayān, the active participle (ism al-fāʿil) indicates firmness and stability of the attribute, whereas the verb form has a weaker indication. This is why we avoid saying 'mustawin' from 'istawā'.
This principle is key to preserving God's transcendence.
3
Examine the supporting parallel
Notice how the Qur'an uses verbs for God's teaching (ʿallama, ʿallamnā) but scholars unanimously forbid calling God 'muʿallim'. This shows consistency in avoiding active participles for divine attributes.
This parallel strengthens the argument.
4
Reflect on the underlying wisdom
Ask yourself: why is it necessary to avoid derived forms? How does this protect against anthropomorphism? Consider how the active participle might imply a settled attribute that does not befit Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرع الثاني : إنه يجب الاحتراز عن التصريف فلا نقول في قوله تعالى : «استوى ، إنه مستوى لما ثبت في علم البيان : أن اسم الفاعل يدل على أن المشتق منه متمكنا ثابتا ومستقرا . أما لفظ الفعل فدلالته على هذا المعنى ضعيفة . والذي يؤكده : أنه ورد في القرآن أنه تعالى علم العباد . فقال : ( الرحمن علم القرآن ) و ( علمك ما لم تكن تعلم ) و ( علمناه من لدنا علما ) ، و ( وعلم آدم الأسماء كلها ) ، ثم أجمعنا على أنه لا يجوز أن يقال الله تعالى : يا معلم . فكذلك ههنا .
The second branch: It is obligatory to avoid derivation, so we do not say regarding His statement, the Most High: 'istawā' (He established Himself), that He is mustawin (established), because it is established in rhetoric (ʿilm al-bayān) that the active participle indicates that the derived form (i.e., the subject) is firmly settled and stable. As for the verb form, its indication of this meaning is weak. And what confirms it is that it came in the Qur'an that the Most High taught servants. He said: 'The Most Merciful taught the Qur'an' and 'He taught you what you did not know' and 'We taught him from Us a knowledge' and 'And He taught Adam the names, all of them.' Then we are unanimously agreed that it is not permissible to say 'O Teacher' (yā muʿallim) of God the Most High. So likewise here.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage presents the second branch: avoiding the derivation (taṣrīf) of ambiguous terms. Specifically, from the verse 'istawā' (He established Himself), one should not say 'mustawin' (the one who establishes Himself in a settled manner). The reason is from the science of rhetoric (ʿilm al-bayān): the active participle (ism al-fāʿil) implies firmness, stability, and settlement (tamakkun, thubūt, istiqrār) of the attribute in its subject. The verb form, on the other hand, has a weaker indication of that settledness. Imam al-Razi supports this with a parallel: the Qur'an uses verbs of teaching (ʿallama, ʿallamnā, etc.) for God, but scholars unanimously agree that it is not permissible to address God as 'muʿallim' (Teacher) as an active participle, because that would imply a fixed attribute of teaching in a way that might not befit God's transcendence. Similarly, 'mustawin' from 'istawā' should be avoided. Thus, the second branch prohibits deriving active participles from ambiguous verbs to prevent implying corporeality or spatial location.

Key Terms
التصريف
اسم الفاعل
علم البيان
متمكنا ثابتا مستقرا
يا معلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that since 'istawā' is used, 'mustawin' is also permissible.
Correction: The active participle carries stronger connotations of settledness and location, which are incompatible with divine transcendence.

Checkpoint
Why does Imam al-Razi forbid saying 'mustawin' (established) for God?
A) Because the word 'mustawin' does not occur in the Qur'an.
B) Because the active participle implies firm settlement and stability, which suggests corporeality.
C) Because the Salaf never used derived forms.
D) Because the verb 'istawā' is ambiguous, but the active participle is clear.

Key Takeaway
Derived verbal forms like active participles should be avoided for ambiguous divine attributes because they imply a degree of settlement unsuitable for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak about God's actions, do you ever use words that imply a human-like settledness, even unintentionally? What does this lesson reveal about how careful you must be with your words?
?
The unanimous agreement on not saying 'O Teacher' for God, despite the Quran using verb forms of teaching, shows that even permissible words can become problematic. Are you willing to submit to scholarly consensus even when it feels stricter than the apparent text?
?
This lesson teaches that the form of a word matters in theology. How often do you reflect on the theological implications of the terms you use for God? What step will you take today to ensure your speech about God remains within the bounds He has set?

The Prohibition of Collecting Ambiguous Terms
Imam Razi forbids gathering multiple ambiguous expressions together.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Razi prohibits gathering multiple ambiguous divine expressions together and how this method safeguards against false anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Gathering many ambiguous terms implies literalism, leading to falsehood; therefore it is prohibited.

In this passage, Imam al-Razi presents a key methodological rule for dealing with ambiguous Qur'anic verses about Allah's attributes. He argues that while a single ambiguous expression can be interpreted metaphorically, accumulating many such expressions gives a false impression of literal meaning, which increases the risk of falling into false beliefs. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its literal translation. Notice the concise style and logical flow.
2
Identify the key terms
Note the terms: 'ambiguous words', 'metaphor' (majāz), 'induction' (istiqrā’). Understand their role.
3
Understand the reasoning
The argument: one or two ambiguous words can be metaphorical, but many together suggest literalism, causing falsehood.
The default in speech is literal, so accumulation overrides the metaphorical possibility.
4
Reflect on the methodology
Consider how this rule protects tanzīh (transcendence) and why the Salaf avoided concatenating ambiguous verses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرع الثالث : إنه لا يجوز جمع الألفاظ المتشابهة . وذلك لأن التلفظ باللفظ الواحد أو باللفظين ، قد يحمل على المجاز . لأن الاستقراء دل على أن الغالب على الكلام : التكلم بالحقيقة . فإذا جمعنا الألفاظ المتشابهة ورويناها دفعة واحدة ، أوهمت كثرتها : أن المراد منها ظواهرها . فكان ذلك الجمع سببا لإيهام زيادة الباطل . وإنه لا يجوز .
The third branch: It is not permissible to collect ambiguous words. That is because uttering a single word or two words may be interpreted metaphorically, since induction (istiqrāʾ) indicates that the predominant mode of speech is literal. So if we collect ambiguous words and narrate them all at once, their abundance suggests that their apparent meanings are intended. Thus that collection becomes a cause for suggesting additional falsehood, and it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage presents the third branch: the prohibition of gathering multiple ambiguous terms together. The reasoning is that when one or two ambiguous expressions are used, they can be interpreted metaphorically (majāz). However, if numerous such expressions are collected and recited together, the sheer quantity gives the impression that the literal (ẓāhir) meanings are intended, because in normal speech the default is literal usage. This collective suggestion increases the danger of falling into false beliefs (tashbīh or tajsīm). Therefore, it is impermissible to combine multiple ambiguous terms in one context. The Salaf would recite each verse individually without concatenating them to avoid this cumulative effect.

Key Terms
جمع الألفاظ المتشابهة
المجاز
الاستقراء
الحقيقة
ظواهرها

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that using multiple ambiguous verses together strengthens the argument for literalism.
Correction: Imam Razi explains that collecting many ambiguous terms actually creates a false impression of literalism and increases the likelihood of false belief, so it is prohibited.

Checkpoint
Why does Imam al-Razi forbid collecting multiple ambiguous divine expressions together?
A) Because it is disrespectful to the Qur'an.
B) Because their abundance suggests they are literal, increasing the chance of false belief.
C) Because the Salaf only used single words.
D) Because it confuses the listener.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Razi's rule against collecting ambiguous terms is a safeguard against inadvertently falling into anthropomorphism by the cumulative weight of literal-sounding expressions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses about Allah's attributes, do you ever catch yourself picturing a hand, a face, or a throne in your mind? How will you actively guard against that literal impression when you hear multiple such verses in one sitting?

?
If someone challenges your belief in Allah's transcendence by piling up verses that sound anthropomorphic, what is your responsibility to yourself and to them? How will you refuse to be swayed by the mere number of texts?

The Principle of Not Separating What the Qur'an Has Joined
Imam Razi forbids separating what the Qur'an has joined, using 'al-Qāhir fawqa ʿibādih' as example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Qur'anic phrase 'al-Qāhir fawqa ʿibādih' must be understood as a whole, and that separating 'fawq' from its context leads to misinterpreting it as spatial direction rather than divine supremacy.

Core Idea
Context defines meaning — the Qur'an's joined phrases cannot be separated.

This lesson builds upon the methodological principle that just as we cannot combine what the Qur'an separates, we also cannot separate what it joins. Imam al-Razi illustrates this with the verse 'al-Qāhir fawqa ʿibādih,' warning against isolating the word 'fawq' from its defining context. By examining the verse, we learn how the words 'al-Qāhir' and 'ʿibādih' together determine the correct interpretation of divine 'above-ness.'

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Focus on the general principle stated at the beginning.
The passage is dense; take your time to absorb each part.
2
Identify the general principle
Note that Imam al-Razi states: 'Just as it is not permissible to collect what is separate, so too it is not permissible to separate what is joined.' This is the core methodological rule.
3
Examine the example
The verse 'al-Qāhir fawqa ʿibādih' serves as an example. See how Razi uses it to demonstrate the principle.
Notice that the verse combines 'al-Qāhir', 'fawqa', and 'ʿibādih' together.
4
Understand the two errors
Razi warns against two separations: (1) extracting 'fawq' alone, and (2) saying 'fawqa ghayrih' instead of 'fawqa ʿibādih'. Understand why each is problematic.
The first error ignores the context of 'al-Qāhir'; the second ignores 'ʿibādih'.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how the mention of 'al-Qāhir' and 'ʿibādih' clarifies that 'above-ness' means subjugation and sovereignty, not spatial direction.
This shows the importance of reading Qur'anic phrases as unified wholes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرع الرابع: إنه كما لا يجوز الجمع بين متفرقه ، فكذلك لا يجوز التفرق بين مجتمعه ، فقوله تعالى : « وهو القاهر فوق عباده ، لا يدل على جواز أن يقال : إنه تعالى فوق . لأنه تعالى لما ذكر القاهر قبله ظهر أن المراد بهذه الفوقية : الفوقية بمعنى القهر ، لا بمعنى الجهة . بل لا يجوز أن يقال : وهو القاهر فوق غيره ، بل ينبغي أن يقال : « فوق عباده ، لأن ذكر العبودية عند وصف الله تعالى بالفوقية ، يدل على أن المراد من تلك الفوقية : فوقية السيادة والإلهية .
The fourth branch: Just as it is not permissible to collect what is separate, so too it is not permissible to separate what is joined. So His statement, the Most High: 'And He is the Subduer over His servants' does not indicate the permissibility of saying that He, the Most High, is 'above' (fawq). Because the Most High mentioned 'al-Qāhir' (the Subduer) before it, it becomes clear that the intended meaning of this 'fawqiyya' (above-ness) is above-ness in the sense of subjugation (qahr), not in the sense of direction (jiha). Rather, it is not permissible to say: 'He is the Subduer above other than Him,' but rather it should be said: 'above His servants,' because mentioning servitude (ʿubūdiyya) when describing God the Most High with above-ness indicates that the intended meaning of that above-ness is the above-ness of sovereignty (siyāda) and divinity (ilāhiyya).
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth branch: the prohibition of separating what the Qur'an has joined. The example is the verse 'wa huwa al-qāhiru fawqa ʿibādih' (And He is the Subduer over His servants). One might be tempted to extract the word 'fawq' (above) and use it alone to describe God, claiming that it denotes spatial elevation. However, Imam al-Razi argues that the verse does not allow such isolation. The word 'fawq' is bound to 'al-qāhir' and 'ʿibādih'. The presence of 'al-qāhir' (the Subduer) shows that the 'above-ness' here means supremacy and domination (qahr), not spatial direction (jiha). Furthermore, if one says 'above other than Him', this removes the context of servitude, which is essential to indicate that the above-ness is one of sovereignty and divinity, not physical height. Thus, the Salaf would not separate the phrase 'fawqa ʿibādih' into 'fawq' alone, because the full expression carries the correct interpretation.

Key Terms
التفرق بين مجتمعه
القاهر
الفوقية
القهر
الجهة
السيادة والإلهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Qur'anic phrase 'fawqa ʿibādih' can be reduced to saying God is 'above' (fawq) without qualification, implying a spatial direction.
Correction: Imam al-Razi shows that the full phrase includes 'al-Qāhir' and 'ʿibādih', which define the above-ness as one of subjugation and sovereignty, not spatial elevation.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi, why is it not permissible to say 'God is above' (fawq) without qualification?
A) Because the word 'fawq' is not used in the Qur'an.
B) Because 'fawq' implies direction, whereas the verse's 'fawqa ʿibādih' means supremacy through the context of 'al-Qāhir' and 'ʿibād'.
C) Because the Salaf never used the word 'fawq'.
D) Because 'fawq' is ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'al-Qāhir fawqa ʿibādih' must be kept intact to convey divine supremacy, not spatial direction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite a verse about Allah's attributes, do you consciously resist the urge to extract a single word and form a mental image, or do you let the full phrase shape your understanding? How will you change this habit after learning Razi's principle?
?
The phrase 'over His servants' links Allah's supremacy to your servitude. Are you living as a true servant, submitting to His authority, or do you use His 'above-ness' as a distant concept that doesn't affect your daily choices? What one change can you make today to act more like a servant?
?
Razi warns against separating what Allah has joined. In your life, have you compartmentalized your faith—keeping some areas for God and others for yourself? What is one area where you need to let the Qur'an's holistic meaning govern your thinking, rather than your own preferences? Commit to a specific step to reintegrate that area under divine guidance.

Active Participle 'Mustawin' and the Analogy with 'Mu'allim'
Al-Razi argues that the active participle 'mustawin' should not be used for Allah, analogously to 'mu'allim'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that the active participle 'mustawin' is not permissible for Allah, based on the analogy with 'mu'allim'.

Core Idea
Active participles imply fixed attributes; Allah is beyond such fixation.

Imam Razi addresses a subtle point in the science of divine attributes. Just because a verb is used in the Quran, it does not mean the corresponding active participle is permissible as a name or description of Allah. He uses the clear example of teaching to draw an analogy, showing that despite multiple Quranic verses attributing teaching to Allah, scholars agree that calling Allah 'Ya Mu'allim' is not allowed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the possible OCR error in the word 'al-na'l' – it may be 'al-fi'l' (the verb).
2
Understand the principle from balaghah
Identify the principle from rhetoric that the active participle indicates that the derived-from is firmly fixed and settled. This is key to the argument.
3
Trace the analogy with 'mu'allim'
Follow how Razi uses the Quranic verses about teaching and the consensus that 'Ya Mu'allim' is not permissible to draw an analogy for 'mustawin'.
Ask yourself: Why does the consensus on 'mu'allim' apply to 'mustawin'?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالى : «استوى»، إنه مستوى. لما ثبت في علم البيان : أن اسم الفاعل يدل على أن المشتق منه متمكنا ثابتا ومستقرا. أما لفظ النعل[؟] فدلالته على هذا المعنى ضعيفة. والذي يؤكده : أنه ورد في القرآن أنه تعالى علم العباد. فقال : «الرحمن علم القرآن» و«وعلمك ما لم تكن تعلم» و«وعلمناه من لدنا علما» و«وعلم آدم الأسماء كلها». ثم أجمعنا على أنه لا يجوز أن يقال الله تعالى : يا معلم. فكذلك مهنا.
He said: 'He istawa', He is mustawin. Because it is established in the science of rhetoric that the active participle indicates that the derived-from is firmly fixed and settled. As for the word al-na'l (sandal?), its indication of this meaning is weak. And what confirms it: that it came in the Quran that He taught the servants. He said: 'The Most Merciful taught the Quran' and 'He taught you what you did not know' and 'We taught him from Us a knowledge' and 'He taught Adam all the names'. Then we are agreed that it is not permissible to say to Allah: O teacher (ya mu'allim). So likewise here.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This is an argument by Imam Razi (may Allah have mercy on him) about the treatment of the active participle derived from the verb 'istawa'. He begins by noting that the verb 'istawa' appears in the Quran, and some might say 'He is mustawin' (established). He then states that it is established in rhetoric (ilm al-bayan) that the active participle indicates that the derived-from (the attribute/state) is firmly fixed and settled. However, he notes that the word 'al-na'l' (likely a corruption of 'al-fi'l' - the verb) has weak indication of this meaning. To confirm the point, he cites multiple Quranic verses where Allah teaches: 'The Most Merciful taught the Quran', 'He taught you what you did not know', 'We taught him knowledge from Us', 'He taught Adam all the names'. Despite these clear verbs of teaching, Muslims are agreed that it is not permissible to address Allah as 'Ya Mu'allim' (O Teacher) as a name. Thus, by analogy, even though the verb 'istawa' is used, one should not coin the active participle 'mustawin' for Allah. This is a precautionary principle in dealing with mutashabihat.

Key Terms
استوى
مستوى
اسم الفاعل
معلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that because Allah is described with a verb, the corresponding noun or participle is also permissible.
Correction: This passage shows that despite multiple Quranic verses attributing teaching to Allah, scholars agree that calling Allah 'Ya Mu'allim' is not permissible. Therefore, the active participle from 'istawa' is likewise not permissible.

Checkpoint
Why does Al-Razi forbid saying 'Ya Mu'allim' to Allah even though Allah teaches in the Quran?
A) Because teaching is an action not an attribute.
B) Because the active participle implies a fixed, established attribute, which is not permissible in this context.
C) Because the word 'Mu'allim' is not found in the Quran.
D) Because Allah dislikes being called teacher.

Key Takeaway
Active participles derived from verbs describing Allah's actions are not allowable if they imply fixed attributes, as shown by the consensus on 'Mu'allim'.

?
Al-Razi uses the consensus on 'Mu'allim' to protect divine transcendence. Have you ever felt embarrassed or hesitant to stop yourself from defining Allah too boldly? What is your heart attached to—being accurate about Allah or feeling comfortable in your own descriptions?
?
The principle here is that active participles imply fixedness, which belies Allah's perfection. Does your heart truly accept that Allah is beyond all human categories, or do you secretly wish He fit neatly into your understanding? What would it cost you to submit to that mystery?

Fourth Branch: Do Not Separate What Is Combined in the Quran
Al-Razi states the fourth branch: prohibition of separating what is combined, with the example of 'fawqa 'ibadihi'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is forbidden to separate a combined Qur'anic phrase like 'fawqa 'ibadihi' from its context, and how this preserves correct divine transcendence.

Core Idea
Don't pick apart what Allah has joined together in His speech.

Imam al-Razi now presents the complementary principle to the previous branch: just as we must not combine separate verses, we must not split combined phrases. The example of 'He is the Subduer above His servants' shows how taking 'above' alone would distort the meaning. Let's see how al-Razi explains this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Notice the structure: rule, then example, then explanation.
2
Identify the rule
The rule is: 'Just as it is not permissible to combine what is separate, so too it is not permissible to separate what is combined.' This is the fourth branch.
This rule guards against proof-texting by taking phrases out of context.
3
Examine the example: 'above His servants'
Al-Razi uses the verse 'He is the Subduer above His servants.' Note that the word 'fawq' is joined with 'al-Qahir' and 'ibadihi'. This context shows the above-ness is one of subjugation, not spatial direction.
If you separate 'fawq' you lose the qualifier that determines its meaning.
4
Understand the consequence of separating
Al-Razi says it is not permissible to say 'above others' instead of 'above His servants' because mentioning servitude indicates the above-ness of sovereignty and divinity.
Changing even one word can alter the theological meaning.
5
Reflect on tanzih
This principle protects Allah's transcendence by ensuring we don't attribute spatial or bodily qualities to Him based on isolated words.
Context is key to understanding mutashabihat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرع الرابع : إنه كما لا يجوز الجمع بين متفرقه ، فكذلك لا يجوز التفرق بين مجتمعه . فقوله تعالى : « وهو القاهر فوق عباده » لا يدل على جواز أن يقال : إنه تعالى فوق . لأنه تعالى لما ذكر القاهر قبله ظهر أن المراد بهذه الفوقية : الفوقية بمعنى القهر ، لا بمعنى الجهة . بل لا يجوز أن يقال : وهو القاهر فوق غيره ، بل ينبغي أن يقال : « فوق عباده » لأن ذكر العبودية عند وصف الله تعالى بالفوقية ، يدل على أن المراد من تلك الفوقية : فوقية السيادة والإلهية .
The fourth branch: Just as it is not permissible to combine what is separate, so too it is not permissible to separate what is combined. So His saying: 'And He is the Subduer above His servants' does not indicate that it is permissible to say that He, exalted, is above in a spatial sense. Because when He mentioned 'the Subduer' before it, it became clear that the intended meaning of this 'above-ness' is the above-ness of subjugation, not the above-ness of direction. Rather, it is not permissible to say: 'And He is the Subduer above others', but one should say: 'above His servants', because mentioning servitude when describing Allah with above-ness indicates that the intended meaning of that above-ness is the above-ness of sovereignty and divinity.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage gives the fourth principle: just as one must not separate what is combined in the Quran (i.e., take a phrase out of its context), so one must not combine what is separate (as in the previous branch). The example is the verse 'He is the Subduer above His servants'. Some might take the word 'fawq' (above) and use it alone to claim that Allah is spatially above. However, the Qur'anic text joins 'fawq' with 'al-Qahir' (the Subduer) and 'ibadihi' (His servants). Since 'al-Qahir' implies subjugation, the 'above-ness' is one of power and control, not spatial direction. Furthermore, if one were to separate the phrase and say 'above others', the specific nuance of 'servitude' (al-ubudiyya) would be lost. The mention of servitude alongside 'above-ness' indicates that the meaning is the above-ness of sovereignty (siyada) and divinity (uluhiyya). Thus, we must preserve the exact wording and context of the Qur'an.

Key Terms
فوقية
فوق عباده
القاهر
فوقية السيادة والإلهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'fawq' in the Quran always implies spatial height, even when combined with other words.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that when 'fawq' is joined with 'al-Qahir' and 'ibadihi', the meaning is not spatial but rather above-ness in power and sovereignty. The context determines the meaning.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Razi, why can one not say 'above others' instead of 'above His servants' in the verse?
A) Because 'others' is a vague term.
B) Because the word 'servants' indicates the above-ness is one of subjugation and sovereignty.
C) Because 'above others' implies a different type of above-ness.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
You must preserve the exact wording and context of Qur'anic descriptions of Allah to avoid misunderstanding His transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'fawqa 'ibadihi' in the Qur'an, do you instinctively think of a physical location for Allah? What subconscious assumptions about Allah's nature are you bringing to the text, and will you now submit to the precise wording He chose?
?
Have you ever used a partial verse to support a theological argument without considering its full context? This lesson demands that you treat every word as intentionally placed—what will you do to ensure you don't separate what Allah has combined?
?
If you truly believe Allah is above His servants in sovereignty and power, how does that change the way you approach Him in your daily life? Are you living as a servant under His subjugation, or are you resisting His authority? What one practice will you start today to embody this 'above-ness' of Allah over you?

The Three Harms of Ambiguous Verses
Razi enumerates the three disastrous effects of ambiguous Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three domains harmed by ambiguous Quranic verses as identified by Imam al-Razi, and the arguments used by skeptics in each domain.

Core Idea
Ambiguous verses, when misinterpreted, damage theology, prophethood, and the divine origin of the Quran.

Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, in his work Asas al-Taqdis, addresses a critical issue: the unintended harmful consequences of mentioning ambiguous (mutashabihat) verses of the Quran. He identifies three distinct areas where these verses become sources of doubt and even outright rejection of Islamic beliefs. As you read the passage, notice how Razi structures his argument and the specific accusations leveled by critics.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Note the three domains Razi lists at the beginning.
The passage is structured as a three-part enumeration.
2
Understand the harm in theology
Focus on the first harm. How do ambiguous verses lead believers to false beliefs about Allah? What does Razi say about their ignorance and false descriptions?
They became ignorant of Allah and described Him with what contradicts divinity and preeternity.
3
Analyze the harm in prophethood
This harm comes from those who understand tanzih (transcendence). How do they use ambiguous verses to attack Muhammad's prophethood? What is their argument?
They claim the prophet should know his Lord perfectly, yet he appears to describe Allah with creaturely attributes.
4
Examine the harm in religious laws
The third harm involves accusations of Quranic corruption. What dilemma does Razi present? Why is this a serious attack on the Quran's integrity?
Either the verses praising the Quran are false, or the ambiguous verses are false.
5
Reflect on the overall message
Consider why Razi begins his chapter with this enumeration. How does it set up the rest of his work on tanzih?
This shows the stakes of mishandling mutashabihat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول في حكم ذكر هذه المتشابهات. اعلم : أن ذكر هذه المتشابهات، صار شبهة عظيمة للخلق في الإلهيات وفي النبوات، وفي الشرائع. أما في الإلهيات: فلأن المصدقين بالقرآن، اعتقدوا في الله تعالى اعتقادات باطلة، حتى صاروا جاهلين بالله تعالى، وواصفين له سبحانه وتعالى بما ينافي الإلهية والقدم. وأما في النبوات: فلأن العارفين بوجوب تنزيه الله تعالى عن هذه الصفات، جعلوا هذا طعنا في نبوة محمد وقالوا: لو كان رسولا حقا من عند الله تعالى لكان أولى المراتب أن يكون عارفا بربه، وحيث لم يعرف ربه بل وصفه بصفات المحدثات، امتنع كونه رسولا حقا. وأما في الشرائع: فلأن فيهم من توسل بذلك إلى الطعن في القرآن. وقالوا: إن القرآن قد غير وبدل، والقرآن الذي أنزل على محمد كان خاليا عن هذه الشبهات. واحتجوا عليه: بأن هذا القرآن مملوء من وصف القرآن بكونه هدى وتبيانا وحكمة وشفاء ونورا. ومن المعلوم بالضرورة: أن هذه الآيات المتشابهات سبب عظيم لضلال الخلق، ووقوعهم في التجسيم والتشبيه، فإما أن تكون الآيات الدالة على كون القرآن نورا، وشفاء: كاذبة. وإما أن تكون الآيات الدالة على التجسيم والتشبيه: باطلة كاذبة.
The first chapter: On the ruling of mentioning these ambiguous verses. Know that mentioning these ambiguous verses has become a great source of doubt for people in matters of divinity, prophethood, and religious laws. As for divinity: because the believers in the Quran held false beliefs about Allah Almighty, until they became ignorant of Allah and described Him, glorified and exalted, with what contradicts divinity and preeternity. As for prophethood: because those who know the necessity of transcending Allah above these attributes made this an objection to the prophethood of Muhammad and said: If he were truly a messenger from Allah, the foremost rank would be that he knows his Lord, and since he did not know his Lord, rather described Him with the attributes of originated things, it is impossible for him to be a true messenger. As for religious laws: because among them some used that to impugn the Quran. They said: The Quran has been altered and changed, and the Quran revealed to Muhammad was free of these ambiguities. They argued that this Quran is filled with descriptions of the Quran as guidance, explanation, wisdom, healing, and light, whereas it is known necessarily that these ambiguous verses are a great cause of people's misguidance and their falling into corporealism and anthropomorphism. So either the verses indicating that the Quran is light and healing are false, or the verses indicating corporealism and anthropomorphism are false and lying.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a classification by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi of the harmful effects that arise from the ambiguous verses (mutashabihat) of the Quran. He states at the outset that mentioning these verses has become a great source of doubt (shubha) for creation in three domains: theology (ilahiyyat), prophethood (nubuwwat), and revealed laws (shara'i'). He then explains each in order.

First, in theology: the people who believe in the Quran, due to misinterpreting ambiguous verses, formed false beliefs about Allah, even describing Him with attributes that contradict true divinity and preeternity (qidam). Thus they became ignorant of Allah's true nature.

Second, in prophethood: those who understand the necessity of tanzih (transcendence) of Allah above all creaturely attributes used the presence of such ambiguous verses in the Quran as an argument against the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). They argued that a true prophet must know his Lord thoroughly, yet Muhammad described Allah with attributes of originated things (sifat al-muhdathat), so he cannot be a true prophet.

Third, in religious laws: some people used these ambiguous verses to claim corruption of the Quran itself. They alleged that the Quran had been altered (ghuyyira wa buddila) and that the original revelation was free from such ambiguities. They argued that the Quran describes itself as guidance, explanation, wisdom, healing, light, etc., yet these same verses cause misguidance, leading people into corporealism (tajsim) and anthropomorphism (tashbih). This creates a dilemma: either the verses praising the Quran are false, or the ambiguous verses themselves are false. Razi presents this as the harmful consequence of mishandling the mutashabihat.

Key Terms
متشابهات
إلهيات
نبوات
شرائع
تنزيه
تجسيم
تشبيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Razi is attacking the Quran itself.
Correction: Razi is exposing the arguments of skeptics in order to refute them, not endorsing their criticisms.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi, what three domains are harmed by the ambiguous verses (mutashabihat)?
A) Theology, ethics, and law
B) Theology, prophethood, and religious laws
C) Prophethood, angels, and eschatology
D) Creation, resurrection, and judgment

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Razi identifies ambiguous verses as a source of doubt in three key areas: theology, prophethood, and the integrity of the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever encountered a verse that seemed to describe Allah in human terms (like 'hand' or 'throne') and felt a flicker of confusion or doubt? How did you handle it? Will you commit to learning the correct interpretation before dismissing it?
?
The skeptics in Razi's time rejected the entire Quran because of a few difficult verses. Are there parts of your faith that you find uncomfortable and quietly ignore or rationalize away? Could your neglect lead you to reject something more fundamental?
?
Razi shows that misinterpreting ambiguous verses can damage your very knowledge of Allah. Are you satisfied with your knowledge of His names and attributes, or have you been careless? What specific step will you take this week to deepen your understanding of tanzih (transcendence)?

The Doubt in Divinity from Ambiguous Verses
Imam Razi presents the doubt in divinity due to ambiguous verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how ambiguous verses have led people to false beliefs about Allah's attributes and divinity.

Core Idea
Ambiguous verses can cause believers to attribute human-like qualities to Allah, undermining His transcendence.

Imam Razi begins by showing how ambiguous verses have become a source of confusion regarding the nature of God. Some believers, taking these verses literally, fell into anthropomorphic misconceptions, describing Allah with qualities that contradict His divinity and pre-eternity. This lesson examines that first doubt.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on divinity
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the claim that believers became ignorant of Allah due to ambiguous verses.
2
Identify the false beliefs
The passage states that believers held 'false beliefs' about Allah, describing Him with what contradicts divinity and pre-eternity. Reflect on what those might be.
These include anthropomorphism (tajsim) and comparing Allah to creation (tashbih).
3
Connect to the broader doubt
Understand that this is the first of three areas where ambiguous verses cause doubt. This sets the stage for the attacks on prophethood and the Quran itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول في حكم ذكر هذه المتشابهات

اعلم : أن ذكر هذه المتشابهات، صار شبهة عظيمة للخلق في الإلهيات وفي النبوات، وفي الشرائع. أما في الإلهيات: فلأن المصدقين بالقرآن، اعتقدوا في الله تعالى اعتقادات باطلة، حتى صاروا جاهلين بالله تعالى، واصفين له سبحانه وتعالى بما ينافي الإلهية والقدم. وأما في النبوات: فلأن العارفين بوجوب تنزيه الله تعالى عن هذه الصفات، جعلوا هذا طعنا في نبوة محمد وقالوا: لو كان رسولا حقا من عند الله تعالى لكان أولى المراتب أن يكون عارفا بربه، وحيث لم يعرف ربه بل وصفه بصفات المحدثات، امتنع كونه رسولا حقا. وأما في الشرائع: فلأن فيهم من توسل بذلك إلى الطعن في القرآن. وقالوا: إن القرآن قد غير وبدل، والقرآن الذي أنزل على محمد كان خاليا عن هذه الشبهات. واحتجوا عليه: بأن هذا القرآن مملوء من وصف القرآن بكونه هدى وتبيانا وحكمة وشفاء ونورا. ومن المعلوم بالضرورة: أن هذه الآيات المتشابهات سبب عظيم لضلال الخلق، ووقوعهم في التجسيم والتشبيه، فإما أن تكون الآيات الدالة على كون القرآن نورا وشفاء كاذبة، وإما أن تكون الآيات الدالة على التجسيم والتشبيه باطلة كاذبة. وعلى التقديرين: فالطعن في القرآن لازم. وأيضا: فهب أنا نحمل هذه الآيات المتشابهة على الكلام بالمجاز لكن من الكلام مجاز وهم لقول باطل، واعتقاد فاسد، وعليه فإنه كان يجب أن نتكلم بذلك الحق على وجه التصريح به، لا بالمتشابهات. ليصير ذلك سببا لزوال الإيهام الباطل. ولا يوجد في القرآن ألفاظ تدل على التنزيه والتوحيد على سبيل التصريح.. فإن قوله: قل هو الله أحد، وقوله: ليس كمثله شيء وهو السميع البصير، لا يدلان على التنزيه إلا دلالة ضعيفة. وكل ذلك يوجب الطعن في القرآن. فهذه حكاية هذه الشبهة في هذا الباب
Chapter One: On the Ruling of Mentioning These Ambiguous Verses

Know that mentioning these ambiguous verses has become a great doubt for the people in matters of divinity, prophethood, and religious laws. As for divinity: because those who believe in the Quran held false beliefs about God Almighty, until they became ignorant of God Almighty, describing Him, may He be glorified and exalted, with what contradicts divinity and pre-eternity. And as for prophethood: because those who know the necessity of declaring God Almighty transcendent above these attributes made this an attack on the prophethood of Muhammad and said: If he had truly been a messenger from God Almighty, the first of ranks would have been that he should know his Lord; and since he did not know his Lord but described Him with the attributes of contingent things, it is impossible for him to be a true messenger. And as for religious laws: because among them are those who used that to attack the Quran. They said: The Quran has been altered and changed, and the Quran that was revealed to Muhammad was free of these doubts. And they argued based on it: that this Quran is full of describing the Quran as being guidance, clarification, wisdom, healing, and light. And it is known necessarily that these ambiguous verses are a great cause for the misguidance of people and their falling into corporealism and anthropomorphism. So either the verses that indicate that the Quran is light and healing are false, or the verses that indicate corporealism and anthropomorphism are false and lying. On both suppositions: the attack on the Quran is necessary. Also: Suppose we interpret these ambiguous verses as metaphorical speech—but metaphorical speech may give the illusion of a false statement and corrupt belief, and therefore it would have been necessary to speak that truth explicitly, not with ambiguous verses, so that it would become a cause for the removal of the false illusion. And there are no words in the Quran indicating transcendence (tanzih) and monotheism (tawhid) explicitly—for His statement: 'Say, He is God, One' and His statement: 'Nothing is like Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing' do not indicate transcendence except with weak indication. And all of that necessitates attacking the Quran. So this is the narration of this doubt in this chapter.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage presents the doubt (shubha) raised by the existence of ambiguous verses (mutashabihat) in the Quran, which opponents use to attack Islam in three areas: divinity (ilahiyyat), prophethood (nubuwwat), and religious laws (shara'i').

First, in divinity: Believers in the Quran, due to anthropomorphic expressions, fell into false beliefs about God, describing Him with attributes that contradict divinity and pre-eternity (qidam), thus becoming ignorant of God.

Second, in prophethood: Those who uphold divine transcendence (tanzih) used these verses to attack Muhammad's prophethood, arguing that a true prophet should know his Lord, but Muhammad described God with the attributes of contingent things (muhdathat).

Third, in religious laws: Some claimed the Quran has been altered, arguing that the original Quran was free of such ambiguous verses. They argued that the Quran describes itself as guidance, clarification, wisdom, healing, and light, yet these ambiguous verses cause misguidance and lead to corporealism (tajsim) and anthropomorphism (tashbih). Therefore, either the verses claiming the Quran is light and healing are false, or the ambiguous verses are false. Either way, the Quran is under attack.

Additionally, even if we interpret ambiguous verses metaphorically, metaphorical speech can give false illusions and corrupt beliefs. It would have been better to state the truth explicitly. Moreover, the Quran lacks explicit verses on transcendence and monotheism; even clear verses like 'Say: He is God, One' and 'Nothing is like Him' only give weak indication of tanzih.

Thus, the doubt concludes that the Quran must be attacked. Imam Razi then notes that this is the narration of the doubt, setting the stage for refutation.

Key Terms
الإلهيات (ilahiyyat)
متشابهات (mutashabihat)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ambiguous verses are harmless and do not affect belief.
Correction: The passage shows that they have caused believers to hold false beliefs about Allah, demonstrating their potential for misguidance.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did believers become due to ambiguous verses?
A) More knowledgeable
B) Ignorant of Allah
C) Stronger in faith
D) Closer to Allah

Key Takeaway
Ambiguous verses have led believers to false conceptions of Allah, contradicting His true nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about Allah that you later realized was based on a verse you misunderstood? How does that realization affect your trust in the Quran's clarity?
?
When you read ambiguous verses, do you feel tempted to attach human-like qualities to Allah? What is the root of that temptation in your heart?
?
What specific belief about Allah do you hold that might contradict His pre-eternity or divinity? Are you willing to examine it today and surrender it for a truer understanding?

The Doubt in Prophethood from Ambiguous Verses
Imam Razi presents the doubt in prophethood due to ambiguous verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how ambiguous verses are used to attack the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
Those who insist on divine transcendence use ambiguous verses to question whether Muhammad could be a true prophet.

The second dimension of the doubt targets prophethood. Those who already know that Allah must be transcendent see the anthropomorphic expressions in the Quran as proof that Muhammad did not truly know his Lord. They argue that a genuine prophet would not describe God with the attributes of created things. This lesson presents that criticism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on prophethood
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the premise: a true prophet must know his Lord correctly.
2
Analyze the argument
The doubt argues that since Muhammad described Allah with attributes of contingent things (muhdathat), he could not be a true prophet. Identify the logical structure.
This is an attack on his knowledge of Allah.
3
Relate to the first doubt
This doubt builds on the first: if believers are misled, then the prophet himself is also misled. See the connection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول في حكم ذكر هذه المتشابهات

اعلم : أن ذكر هذه المتشابهات، صار شبهة عظيمة للخلق في الإلهيات وفي النبوات، وفي الشرائع. أما في الإلهيات: فلأن المصدقين بالقرآن، اعتقدوا في الله تعالى اعتقادات باطلة، حتى صاروا جاهلين بالله تعالى، واصفين له سبحانه وتعالى بما ينافي الإلهية والقدم. وأما في النبوات: فلأن العارفين بوجوب تنزيه الله تعالى عن هذه الصفات، جعلوا هذا طعنا في نبوة محمد وقالوا: لو كان رسولا حقا من عند الله تعالى لكان أولى المراتب أن يكون عارفا بربه، وحيث لم يعرف ربه بل وصفه بصفات المحدثات، امتنع كونه رسولا حقا. وأما في الشرائع: فلأن فيهم من توسل بذلك إلى الطعن في القرآن. وقالوا: إن القرآن قد غير وبدل، والقرآن الذي أنزل على محمد كان خاليا عن هذه الشبهات. واحتجوا عليه: بأن هذا القرآن مملوء من وصف القرآن بكونه هدى وتبيانا وحكمة وشفاء ونورا. ومن المعلوم بالضرورة: أن هذه الآيات المتشابهات سبب عظيم لضلال الخلق، ووقوعهم في التجسيم والتشبيه، فإما أن تكون الآيات الدالة على كون القرآن نورا وشفاء كاذبة، وإما أن تكون الآيات الدالة على التجسيم والتشبيه باطلة كاذبة. وعلى التقديرين: فالطعن في القرآن لازم. وأيضا: فهب أنا نحمل هذه الآيات المتشابهة على الكلام بالمجاز لكن من الكلام مجاز وهم لقول باطل، واعتقاد فاسد، وعليه فإنه كان يجب أن نتكلم بذلك الحق على وجه التصريح به، لا بالمتشابهات. ليصير ذلك سببا لزوال الإيهام الباطل. ولا يوجد في القرآن ألفاظ تدل على التنزيه والتوحيد على سبيل التصريح.. فإن قوله: قل هو الله أحد، وقوله: ليس كمثله شيء وهو السميع البصير، لا يدلان على التنزيه إلا دلالة ضعيفة. وكل ذلك يوجب الطعن في القرآن. فهذه حكاية هذه الشبهة في هذا الباب
Chapter One: On the Ruling of Mentioning These Ambiguous Verses

Know that mentioning these ambiguous verses has become a great doubt for the people in matters of divinity, prophethood, and religious laws. As for divinity: because those who believe in the Quran held false beliefs about God Almighty, until they became ignorant of God Almighty, describing Him, may He be glorified and exalted, with what contradicts divinity and pre-eternity. And as for prophethood: because those who know the necessity of declaring God Almighty transcendent above these attributes made this an attack on the prophethood of Muhammad and said: If he had truly been a messenger from God Almighty, the first of ranks would have been that he should know his Lord; and since he did not know his Lord but described Him with the attributes of contingent things, it is impossible for him to be a true messenger. And as for religious laws: because among them are those who used that to attack the Quran. They said: The Quran has been altered and changed, and the Quran that was revealed to Muhammad was free of these doubts. And they argued based on it: that this Quran is full of describing the Quran as being guidance, clarification, wisdom, healing, and light. And it is known necessarily that these ambiguous verses are a great cause for the misguidance of people and their falling into corporealism and anthropomorphism. So either the verses that indicate that the Quran is light and healing are false, or the verses that indicate corporealism and anthropomorphism are false and lying. On both suppositions: the attack on the Quran is necessary. Also: Suppose we interpret these ambiguous verses as metaphorical speech—but metaphorical speech may give the illusion of a false statement and corrupt belief, and therefore it would have been necessary to speak that truth explicitly, not with ambiguous verses, so that it would become a cause for the removal of the false illusion. And there are no words in the Quran indicating transcendence (tanzih) and monotheism (tawhid) explicitly—for His statement: 'Say, He is God, One' and His statement: 'Nothing is like Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing' do not indicate transcendence except with weak indication. And all of that necessitates attacking the Quran. So this is the narration of this doubt in this chapter.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage presents the doubt (shubha) raised by the existence of ambiguous verses (mutashabihat) in the Quran, which opponents use to attack Islam in three areas: divinity (ilahiyyat), prophethood (nubuwwat), and religious laws (shara'i').

First, in divinity: Believers in the Quran, due to anthropomorphic expressions, fell into false beliefs about God, describing Him with attributes that contradict divinity and pre-eternity (qidam), thus becoming ignorant of God.

Second, in prophethood: Those who uphold divine transcendence (tanzih) used these verses to attack Muhammad's prophethood, arguing that a true prophet should know his Lord, but Muhammad described God with the attributes of contingent things (muhdathat).

Third, in religious laws: Some claimed the Quran has been altered, arguing that the original Quran was free of such ambiguous verses. They argued that the Quran describes itself as guidance, clarification, wisdom, healing, and light, yet these ambiguous verses cause misguidance and lead to corporealism (tajsim) and anthropomorphism (tashbih). Therefore, either the verses claiming the Quran is light and healing are false, or the ambiguous verses are false. Either way, the Quran is under attack.

Additionally, even if we interpret ambiguous verses metaphorically, metaphorical speech can give false illusions and corrupt beliefs. It would have been better to state the truth explicitly. Moreover, the Quran lacks explicit verses on transcendence and monotheism; even clear verses like 'Say: He is God, One' and 'Nothing is like Him' only give weak indication of tanzih.

Thus, the doubt concludes that the Quran must be attacked. Imam Razi then notes that this is the narration of the doubt, setting the stage for refutation.

Key Terms
النبووات (nubuwwat)
تنزيه (tanzih)
صفات المحدثات (attributes of contingent things)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The doubt is only about God's nature, not about prophethood.
Correction: This passage explicitly uses ambiguous verses to attack Muhammad's prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to the doubt, what does the fact that Muhammad described God with attributes of contingent things prove?
A) He was a true prophet
B) He did not know his Lord
C) He knew his Lord well
D) He was a great scholar

Key Takeaway
Ambiguous verses are used to argue that Muhammad lacked proper knowledge of Allah, thus challenging his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed someone's Islamic knowledge because they used simple or anthropomorphic language about Allah, assuming that true knowledge requires abstract tanzih? How does the doubt presented in this lesson challenge that assumption, and what will you do about it?
?
If you were faced with the argument that Muhammad (saw) could not be a true prophet because he described Allah with human-like attributes, would your immediate reaction be to defend or to doubt? What does your answer reveal about the strength of your own conviction, and what step will you take to fortify it?
?
The doubters in this passage claim to be the true knowers of God's transcendence. Are you ever tempted to feel superior in your understanding of Islam compared to others who use simpler expressions? How can this lesson protect you from that pride, and what concrete action will you take to check your heart?

The Doubt in Religious Law and the Quran's Integrity
Imam Razi presents the doubt in religious law and the Quran's authenticity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how ambiguous verses are used to attack the Quran's authenticity and claim it has been altered.

Core Idea
Ambiguous verses are said to contradict the Quran's own description of itself as guidance and light, leading to the charge of alteration.

The third dimension of the doubt targets religious law (Islamic teachings) and the Quran itself. Opponents argue that the presence of ambiguous verses contradicts the Quran's claim to be clear guidance. They either claim the Quran has been altered or that its clear verses are false. Additionally, they argue that even metaphorical interpretation doesn't solve the problem, and that the Quran lacks explicit verses on transcendence. This lesson covers these interconnected doubts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on religious law
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the two main arguments: alteration of the Quran and the inconsistency with its own description.
2
Understand the alteration claim
Some claim the original Quran was free of ambiguous verses, implying the current Quran has been changed. Identify the evidence they use.
They use the Quran's self-description as clear guidance.
3
Analyze the metaphorical argument
Even if we interpret metaphorically, the doubt says metaphorical speech can still create false illusions. It would have been better to speak explicitly.
4
Note the claim about explicit verses
They claim that even clear verses like 'Say: He is God, One' do not strongly indicate transcendence. This conclusion attacks the Quran's eloquence.

Divine Transcendence
beginner
4 min
Common Terms Do Not Imply Anthropomorphism
Clarifies that sharing terms does not force tashbih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that shared attributes between God and creation do not necessitate tashbih (anthropomorphism) because similarity in some respects does not mean essential likeness.

Core Idea
Shared words do not mean shared essence.

A common accusation against those who affirm attributes for God is that they commit tashbih by using the same terms for God and creation. The author begins by stating that such commonality is undisputed, but it does not force anthropomorphism. He then explains his group's position: they affirm some similarity in attributes but believe God is utterly unique in essence, so the charge is false.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice how the author lists many terms and then makes his point about similarity.
This paragraph is setting up the issue.
2
Identify the key claim
The author asserts that using the same words for God and creation does not make one an anthropomorphist. The reason is that similarity in some respects does not necessitate essential likeness.
This is the core of the lesson.
3
Understand the opponents' position
The author quotes the opponents' argument: they admit to affirming some similarity (in forms and attributes) but insist God's essence is different, so calling them 'anthropomorphists' is false.
This shows the debate context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم: أنه لا نزاع في أن لفظ: الموجود، والشيء، والواحد، والذات، والمعلوم، والمذكور، والعالم، والقادر، والحى، والمريد، والسميع، والبصير، والمتكلم، والباقي: واقع على الحق سبحانه وتعالى، وعلى خلقه. مثبت بما ذكرنا: أن المشابهة من بعض الوجوه لا توجب أن يكون قائله موصوفاً بأنه مشبه الله تعالى بالخلق، وبأنه مشبه. ونحن لا نثبت المشابهة بينه وبين خلقه، إلا في بعض الصور (٥٨) والصفات، إلا أنا نعتقد أنه تعالى، وإن كان جسماً، إلا أنه بخلاف سائر الأجسام في ذاته وحقيقته. فثبت: أن إطلاق اسم المشبه على هذه الطائفة: كذب وزور. هذا جملة كلامهم في هذا الباب.
واعلم: أن حاصل هذا الكلام من جانبنا: أنا قد دللنا في القسم الأول من هذا الكتاب على أن الأجسام متماثلة في تمام الماهية. فلو كان الباري تعالى جسماً لزم أن يكون مثلاً لهذه الأجسام في تمام الماهية (٢٥٩). وحينئذ يكون القول بالتشبيه لازماً. أما ما لم يدل الدليل على الشيء في الموجودية والعالمية والقادرية، فإنه لا يوجب تماثلها في تمام الماهية. فظهر الفرق. (وبالله التوفيق) (٦١)
And know: there is no dispute that the terms: the existent, the thing, the one, the essence, the known, the mentioned, the knowing, the powerful, the living, the willing, the hearing, the seeing, the speaking, and the eternal: apply to the Truth, exalted and high, and to His creation. Established by what we have mentioned: that similarity in some respects does not necessitate that its speaker be described as one who likens God, exalted, to creation, and as one who anthropomorphizes. And we do not affirm similarity between Him and His creation, except in some forms (58) and attributes, except that we believe that He, exalted, though He is a body, is nevertheless different from all other bodies in His essence and reality. So it is established: that applying the name 'anthropomorphist' to this group is falsehood and slander. This is the gist of their words on this topic.
And know: that the substance of this speech from our side: we have proven in the first section of this book that bodies are similar in the entirety of essence. So if the Exalted Creator were a body, it would necessitate that He be similar to these bodies in the entirety of essence (259). Then the claim of anthropomorphism would be necessary. As for what evidence does not indicate about a thing in existence and knowledge and power, it does not necessitate their similarity in the entirety of essence. So the difference appears. (And with Allah is success) (61).
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage addresses the charge of tashbih (anthropomorphism) against those who affirm certain attributes for God. It is a two-part argument: first, the author presents the position of the opponents (or a clarification). He states that there is no dispute that many terms (like existent, knower, etc.) apply both to God and to creation. This commonality does not imply that the one who uses these terms is guilty of likening God to creation. In fact, the author asserts that he and his group do not affirm similarity between God and creation except in some forms and attributes, but they believe that even if God is described as a 'body' (in their theological framework), He is different from all other bodies in His essence and reality. Therefore, calling them 'anthropomorphists' is false. This is a summary of their view.

Then the author presents his own proof from the first section of the book: he had already demonstrated that bodies are identical in their complete essence. If God were a body, He would be like all other bodies in essence, which would indeed make the charge of tashbih necessary. However, the attributes like existence, knowledge, and power that are applied to God without evidence of essential similarity do not necessitate that God is like other beings in essence. Thus, the difference between common attributes and essential likeness is clear. The passage concludes with 'And with Allah is success.'

Key Terms
موجود
عالم
قادر
تشبيه
مشابهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If we say God is 'knowing' and humans are 'knowing', we are likening God to humans in essence.
Correction: The author clarifies that similarity in some attributes does not imply essential likeness. God's knowledge is unique and not like human knowledge in essence.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the common application of terms like 'existent' and 'knowing' to both God and creation NOT imply?
A) That God is similar to creation in essence.
B) That those who use these terms are anthropomorphists.
C) That God is different from creation.
D) That the terms are used metaphorically.

Key Takeaway
Shared terms between God and creation do not force essential similarity or anthropomorphism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you describe God as 'knowing' or 'powerful', do you catch yourself imagining a limited, human-like knowledge or power? How does this lesson's insistence on essential uniqueness challenge the way you think about God's attributes in your daily worship?
?
Have you ever felt uncomfortable using the word 'body' for God, even while reading the Quran? After this lesson, what is the real reason you should not reject it outright if it is affirmed by scripture, while still maintaining God's incomparability?
?
Think of a time you accused someone of anthropomorphism because they used a word for God that seemed too familiar. Could that accusation have been a slander (as the author says 'falsehood and slander')? What would you need to check before making such an accusation?

Why Anthropomorphism Would Follow from Essential Likeness
Proves that if God were a body, tashbih would result, but common attributes don't imply essential likeness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's proof that if God were a body in the same sense as other bodies, tashbih would be necessary, but attributes like knowledge do not entail essential similarity.

Core Idea
Essential similarity is the real issue, not common attributes.

After presenting the opponents' defense, the author now gives his own reasoning from the first part of his book. He had proved that all bodies are identical in their complete essence. Hence, if God were a body, He would be essentially like other bodies—this would truly be tashbih. However, attributes like existence and knowledge do not by themselves prove essential likeness, so the charge does not stick.

Guided Path
1
Read the second paragraph
Read the Arabic and translation for the author's argument. Notice the structure: 'we have proven... so if... then... as for... so the difference appears'.
This is a logical argument.
2
Understand the proof
The author refers to his earlier proof that bodies are identical in complete essence. If God were a body, He would share that identity, making tashbih necessary. This shows that the real threat is essential likeness, not shared attributes.
Focus on the conditional 'if... then'.
3
Distinguish between attributes and essence
The author says that attributes like 'existent', 'knowing', etc., do not imply complete essential similarity. They are common without forcing tashbih.
This is the key distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم: أنه لا نزاع في أن لفظ: الموجود، والشيء، والواحد، والذات، والمعلوم، والمذكور، والعالم، والقادر، والحى، والمريد، والسميع، والبصير، والمتكلم، والباقي: واقع على الحق سبحانه وتعالى، وعلى خلقه. مثبت بما ذكرنا: أن المشابهة من بعض الوجوه لا توجب أن يكون قائله موصوفاً بأنه مشبه الله تعالى بالخلق، وبأنه مشبه. ونحن لا نثبت المشابهة بينه وبين خلقه، إلا في بعض الصور (٥٨) والصفات، إلا أنا نعتقد أنه تعالى، وإن كان جسماً، إلا أنه بخلاف سائر الأجسام في ذاته وحقيقته. فثبت: أن إطلاق اسم المشبه على هذه الطائفة: كذب وزور. هذا جملة كلامهم في هذا الباب.
واعلم: أن حاصل هذا الكلام من جانبنا: أنا قد دللنا في القسم الأول من هذا الكتاب على أن الأجسام متماثلة في تمام الماهية. فلو كان الباري تعالى جسماً لزم أن يكون مثلاً لهذه الأجسام في تمام الماهية (٢٥٩). وحينئذ يكون القول بالتشبيه لازماً. أما ما لم يدل الدليل على الشيء في الموجودية والعالمية والقادرية، فإنه لا يوجب تماثلها في تمام الماهية. فظهر الفرق. (وبالله التوفيق) (٦١)
And know: there is no dispute that the terms: the existent, the thing, the one, the essence, the known, the mentioned, the knowing, the powerful, the living, the willing, the hearing, the seeing, the speaking, and the eternal: apply to the Truth, exalted and high, and to His creation. Established by what we have mentioned: that similarity in some respects does not necessitate that its speaker be described as one who likens God, exalted, to creation, and as one who anthropomorphizes. And we do not affirm similarity between Him and His creation, except in some forms (58) and attributes, except that we believe that He, exalted, though He is a body, is nevertheless different from all other bodies in His essence and reality. So it is established: that applying the name 'anthropomorphist' to this group is falsehood and slander. This is the gist of their words on this topic.
And know: that the substance of this speech from our side: we have proven in the first section of this book that bodies are similar in the entirety of essence. So if the Exalted Creator were a body, it would necessitate that He be similar to these bodies in the entirety of essence (259). Then the claim of anthropomorphism would be necessary. As for what evidence does not indicate about a thing in existence and knowledge and power, it does not necessitate their similarity in the entirety of essence. So the difference appears. (And with Allah is success) (61).
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage addresses the charge of tashbih (anthropomorphism) against those who affirm certain attributes for God. It is a two-part argument: first, the author presents the position of the opponents (or a clarification). He states that there is no dispute that many terms (like existent, knower, etc.) apply both to God and to creation. This commonality does not imply that the one who uses these terms is guilty of likening God to creation. In fact, the author asserts that he and his group do not affirm similarity between God and creation except in some forms and attributes, but they believe that even if God is described as a 'body' (in their theological framework), He is different from all other bodies in His essence and reality. Therefore, calling them 'anthropomorphists' is false. This is a summary of their view.

Then the author presents his own proof from the first section of the book: he had already demonstrated that bodies are identical in their complete essence. If God were a body, He would be like all other bodies in essence, which would indeed make the charge of tashbih necessary. However, the attributes like existence, knowledge, and power that are applied to God without evidence of essential similarity do not necessitate that God is like other beings in essence. Thus, the difference between common attributes and essential likeness is clear. The passage concludes with 'And with Allah is success.'

A) Calling God 'knowing'.
B) Proving that God is a body identical in essence to other bodies.
C) Using the term 'body' in any sense.
D) Affirming that God has attributes.

Key Takeaway
Essential identity, not shared attributes, is the criterion for tashbih.
